O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the essence of medical knowledge assembled together with its fulfillment, and finished it through its explanations and revelations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in my vision, I came to know that I should complete this with this manual, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is well-established in our region and unknown everywhere else, so has knowledge been lost and surgery stripped down to bare, and nothing remains from it that wasn't recorded in books by the ancients whose hands have performed surgeries.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And out of this comes error and vanity, and minds are closed off and knowledge is lost.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It appears that I should revive this treatise together with its order according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will come together with the forms of iron cauteries, and other tools for working, with the adjustment of declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled masters are found in our times, the art of medicine has been lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who intervenes to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows how to judge the parts, and their shapes and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews, and the number of bones, and their disposition and of moving and static veins, and where they exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus says Hippocrates that it is much easier to avoid illness than to treat it with medicine; and similarly in the art of manual skills.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We are telling you at the beginning of this book that if someone is not aware of the things previously mentioned, they may make mistakes and mislead people; just as I have seen many times where those who interfere with this science abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	And I have seen a fool who performed an operation on a woman's neck to remove a sore or swelling, and cut into the arteries in her neck. Because so much blood came out that the woman died from her own hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a large stone in the body of an old man, and the stone was large. He removed a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to help draw blood, and saw the position of the body and the size of the stone, and if they had removed it while he was alive, he would have died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where a cure took on the task of treating our lord's leg which was broken, and with the breakage came an injury; and the doctors full of ignorance caused the break to occur in the wound, causing it to become inflamed by strong winds, and did not allow the wound any rest from bleeding, and allowed it to happen like this for months; and he instructed them not to ever cause such harm again; and waited until the leg was completely swollen up to the feet and then went towards ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was summoned to come to him, and I quickly came to relieve his leg; and when I heard that it had been dislocated so much that he felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every path of corruption had already been confirmed or member, and one could not heal it; and the corruption would continue to spread within the body as long as the limbs were completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And look at a second sore which collapses an abscess that is deeply embedded, and then inflames through the wickedness of her lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is full of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron if it isn't in its place where one can remove all that has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear children, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, an area where there are dangers in multiple situations; and I will show each one of these divisions within this book where it has fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary that you keep this in mind, so that no one can harm you. Take your weapons into consideration, and treat your illnesses lightly yet firmly, and use the best way possible so that with God's grace you come to health and become strong; and leave the terrifying diseases without complaint of sickness; and remove from yourself those who cause you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can go from this world to glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiens warns in none of his admonishments: "Do not treat illness wrongly, lest you be called foolish.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters deal with fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and these chapters are arranged from the head to the stones; and about the forms of instruments, and the metals of cauteries, and all that is necessary for the operation.

The third chapters concern the restoration of dislocations and twists, as well as similar matters; these chapters are arranged from head to stones, and include descriptions of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remind ourselves of the work, it is necessary for me to describe the quality and harm of each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid, and harm, are the longest word and most subtle science and secrets in response; and many wise ones spoke about this, agreeing with it. And they provided little to me through their words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery universally applies to all types of skin where there is matter present, considering that there are two types of compositions: one being hot with matter, and another being dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the composition that is both hot and dry with matter present, they devised a plan and said that the fire cautery is great aid; while others said the opposite: that the fire cautery only works for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be treated with hot illnesses by heat or drying; and it's said that he who says otherwise that the cautery gives great aid to hot and dry diseases that come into men's bodies.

Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion by means of experimentation.

Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come out anywhere except on the body part that is burned, and it does not harm any other body part.

The fiery medicines spread from one part to another by moving away, causing diseases of sickness healing in the affected parts; and by chance, the patient's body with its height and due to the goodness of its substance doesn't do this if there isn't excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this is what I have found through experimentation and the longevity of my service and study in the art, which corresponds to the truth of things. And for this, I apologize for the length of speech, because I do not want to take away from you the secret that lies with fire and the quality of work, how it relieves diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says by demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they determined when the cauterizations should be done, and studied their effects.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the harms occurring are minimized by the help of the cautery; and moreover, if the cauterizations are due to necessary pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm would occur to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like the foolish ones do, my dear child; because a disease cured by cauterization does not bring back what was lost. And they say it this way: but that is not entirely true, for cauterizations are only medicine that changes the complexion and dries up the fluids that cause pain, and their value lies in expediting one's strength and in the virtue of their work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the ability exists that diseases occur according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its virtue; and they gather in him the excesses through the consumption of meats and similar things, if not treated with cauterization where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauterizations for pain, and similar things, so that such pain does not recur; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And no one understands why cauteries are called after medicine, it's hard to see; but they do not believe that cauteries can follow medicine afterwards. However, their understanding is false, and in cautery being the latter of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they don't work, then we administer our cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it's correct to say that cauteries are indeed the latter part of medicine, not according to the understanding of people there.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauteries are more effective than iron ones, and they mentioned this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance. They also stated that gold cautery doesn't cause decay, which is not true as I have proven it; and found out that it does occur in some people. And gold cauteries work better than iron ones, just like they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know that it is heated by the color of gold and it cools immediately; and if you heat it too much; then put it in fire; and so there is enough prevention.

dou cautere olivaire	Use an olive pincer cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	A fire cautery is effective against moisture and cold on the head. There are two of them that we perform due to the cause of an illness called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head as in eyes, ears, and because of numerous dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially all diseases coming from cold such as paralysis, soda (which seems to be a typo, possibly meant to refer to something like apoplexy), and apoplexy-like illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient's condition is purified by a dissolving medicine altering the head. Either three times or four times, depending on how much the properties and the heat and the habituation to the patient's condition can bear; and then washes the head with the patient afterwards.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him lie down with his hands crossed between your hands, and place his hands on the palm of his hand; after put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two nostrils; and let it be where your middle fingers reach, if it bleeds from there, heat up the cautery which is called 'olivare', with this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the joint with ink, and when you descend and apply pressure little by little while twisting your hand; then raise your hand alone, and check if you see bone. After that, place on top of cotton soaked in butter; let it stay until the scab is removed; afterwards treat the wound with tetracycline ointment until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they were told by the old ones that the more time an open wound stays exposed, the more it will purify; and due to this, movements are taken.

Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other says that when using a cautery, one should keep it in place there and push so forcefully that it lifts part of the bone as wide as half a hazelnut because this is what women do with their needles to let body fluids flow out; and one should leave the wound exposed for an extended period. Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be entirely good for all things; except when there is a way for fear in some people. dou cautere dou chief	Instruct the fire cautery to operate upon the malady, commanding it to let the hairs grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in part of the head and spreads until it reaches the eye, and the disease is cured by purging medicines, and various other treatments have been done as I've mentioned in the division of diseases, but none are benefiting: then upon this I perform cauteries according to two methods, that is, with medicine for ague and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine-based cauteries consist of taking a spoonful of vinegar, and using the peel and the inside of it for two parts of each shoulder. You then apply this mixture on the area where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the spoonful of vinegar under the skin; once it is placed there, make sure to tie and tighten it well and leave it like that for 12 hours; after which remove the vinegar bandage and let the wound heal for two days or three. Then apply a butter-soaked cloth until the soreness exits.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment as long as it is sound; and if you see fit to use some of the burning medicines that I have written or the first treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery follows this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery as shown here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a bell, having .i. point of curvature, and halfway through there is a small appearance; and place it over the painful area, hold your hand steady and gently move the iron for a bit, until half of the thickness of the skin is burned; then lift your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, when it's done, let out abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After this, put wool in place of the lint, and apply it over the affected area for three days; then replace with wet cotton soaked in butter, and continue to treat the area with ointment as long as it is sound; and if you want to cauterize this migraine using the cautery that is called "cultellare" (a type of hot iron), apply at the whole tip, but take care not to cover the artery in this migraine which isn't old.
de emigraine	Of a headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat headache as we have previously explained in the divisions of diseases, and if it doesn't improve, and you observe that the cauterization methods previously described in medicine don't work on him, then it's necessary for you to heat up the cauterizing tool known as 'cultellare' until it turns white; and so when there is a line half an inch long from the head, and your hand operates once, and you apply pressure ensuring not to cut the artery and stopping before reaching the bone; and beware of the jaw clenching when eating, and only let the tongue and throat be attentive during this phase, and avoid spasms that could harm the patient. And be cautious about blood leakage from the artery if it's cut or if the operation causes much fear in someone who is not trained and experienced, and who isn't aware of these procedures; and leave the work halfway done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery has been cut, and show you its correct location in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations don't help with the illness and the patient is suffering, apply the cauterization in the middle of the head as we have instructed, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you observe this, administer the cauterizer as described or from the chapter on extracting arteries, using a cauterizer that has two blades. And these cauterizers are better than others and more effective.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold causes pain in the ear, and treatments involving solvents and other remedies that we have discussed in this section are applied, and if the pain persists, then prepare this type of cautery called "points", as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying points around the entire ear, or around both sides where the pain is felt, move away from the base of the ear soon after marking its position; place ten points around each ear. After this, treat the area until it has healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the agony of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Pain that should be cured by a cautery does not include those that move from blood flow, as we have said in the sections on diseases; and no cautery should be done for symptoms that come from scarring and skin rashes.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this kind of pain that originates from water flow and head discharges, as well as gargling, and this does not work, then it is necessary for you to apply the cautery with three applications: one at the root of the ear, and another slightly outside the temple area, and the third in adjusting the two lips; place the cautery on the healthy part that opens, and cauterize that spot above the ear's root up to a bit under the head of the ear, and do the same for the temple as long as it is about one pace; let the cautery be placed there until half of the skull is burned; this is how you should use the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the appearance of cutaneous ailments as we described earlier, but it's a bit more subtle and requires that the knives be slightly thicker; after treating the area in the manner I've described previously, do so until it heals properly.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with a long-lasting apoplexy and you are treating it as we have said, and it doesn't help at all, and the patients do not have fever, then you should apply four cauteries: two on each of the two temple areas, one under the chin, and one where the head is located that is referred to as 'vassel' as we mentioned before. And perform the last cautery over the mouth of the stomach; treat it as we said beforehand.
de litargie	From Liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, you should give the patient large pills and mastic tablets that purify the brain; afterwards, wipe off the head of the patient completely, and then place the sinapical plaster under the back part of the head as written or described in how to apply plasters; and this is how to perform the cautery: do it just as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it proceeds thusly, well done; and if not, let three fire cauteries be performed descending from the head to the collarbone, with an interval of one finger's width between each cautery. And treat them as others are treated, and if you see that they adjust, and the patient is suffering, let a third cautery be applied in the middle; and should it require further treatment, two more on the two horns, and treat until they are healed; and make of those cauteries which are called 'olive-shaped', as I have previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	From the cooling of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to cleanse the head of years and what we have mentioned before; after soothing the head with the patient, then let a fire cautery be applied around the wound, on each horn, one behind and three on the spine beneath the neck; and if you need more treatment, and the area is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease continues, apply four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave it until the worst kind of heat is burned away, then lift your hand; after that treat until it is healed, and make of those cauteries which are called 'olive-shaped', as we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	From epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use the cautery if they are phlegmatic, and first need to modify the head with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section where the patients have large issues and suffer from medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the child can't endure it, make them gargle and chew, modifying the head often with good meats; after that you place the neck halfway, and I apply one fire according to what we have said before, and one fire on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is overactive and suffering, I apply fires as I told in those who are paralysed and have a softening of their body, on the spine at the back and neck, and let the olive fires be done according to the method that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	And if the illness is in a child, then you apply one subtle fire according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy are the excesses or the moist substances corrupted and large, then the metal cautery of the fire cautery as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to the cause of melancholy is the excess declining into melancholy, and there is moisture in the body's organs, then it should drink something so that the brain becomes purified, according to what was explained previously in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have removed the head of the illness; after this make one and a half pieces of well-made linen, like one circle, put it around the head; if there is any complaint from the organs, place them in their correct position, held firmly all around; then present the liniment, and apply it with butter of old beeswax; heat it over fire until you know whether it can be tolerated or not; after this pour out the circle containing the head, let it cool down; and do this for each organ once a week using different management, as long as there is no further complaint.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see it being cauterized, do so by making several marks across the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautering moistens the brain greatly; and then place wet cotton on butter and lard.
de l’awe des eulz	of the fear of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When fear first comes to the eyes through the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and continue to instruct the patient to drink something that purifies the head, and protects it from all moisture, and make them sweat or take baths several times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After having him clean his head and apply cauterization to it, and have him undergo two cauterizations on the two temples once his fear has subsided completely in both eyes or when it subsides in one eye; then take care of every application around the skull for all veins and arteries that are within it, and perform each cauterization long according to the width of the temple; and guard against bleeding out, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it at a point with the same method as before.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions in the cautery, how to apply it properly; and whenever a cautery or cauterization is done, do not perform it over the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the path of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed, and are located on the veins, or beneath the arteries that are visible outside of the head; and it can be seen that they are cold excesses of phlegm. Therefore, do as I have said at the beginning of this work for the treatment of these things: 1) apply the cautery to the forehead, and 2) two cauterizations on each temple, and 3) two cauterizations or application over the bones below; and if more is needed, carefully apply the cautery up from the eyebrows with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the path of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you apply the medicines according to what we have said in the division, and if they do not benefit, then give three raw chickens to the patient to drink. After he has consumed this, take his head, and perform a cautery or olive oil cautery; and make two cauteries using the ‘clavilis’ type of cautery on each of four nostrils, slightly over the hairline; and be cautious not to touch the artery when you perform this procedure.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "oily".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which the form is:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it takes two cauteries on each of the two nipples as long as they are present; and do not release your hand until only a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hairs that prick at their base
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	None of the times has it been that the hair at their nipples turns into the armpits, and pricks them, then one performs cauteries according to two ways: namely with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and equal, then instruct the patient to be in a state of health; afterward, on the page describing the eyes, draw a figure that looks like a leaf of myrtle, and make it resemble the beginning of the sign with the hairs. Then place moistened cotton infused with egg whites and garlic paste on the eye, then heat up the cautery which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have drawn gradually and many times so that it burns in the eye area, and signs of health are as follows: when you see the paper retracting, and hairs raised at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave thus for three days. Then place moistened cotton dipped in butter until the scorching is removed; afterwards apply ointment until it is clean.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And when hair and paper become soft again, then reapply the cautery to that same area as you did initially. If hair has fallen out, then cauterize until the paper is raised back to its natural position and evenly distributed, without touching the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	In the treatment of heated cauterization, you should instruct the patient to let their hair grow until they are long and even, then create a shape from parchment like the leaf of myrtle; next take one part each of French soap and fresh oil, combine them well; then apply it quickly without allowing it to cool, after which place on the form that matches the leaf of myrtle and put onto paper with your eyes; if the illness lasts for only half an hour, then cut open halfway, and if both are also affected; place a piece of wet cotton inside each eye akin to an egg; let the patient's head stay in your healthy position and apply your fingers on the medicine, squeezing once every time the patient feels the irritation from the medicine, as they feel it just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if you apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the excision is past, lift up the arm, and reward it if you see that the paper has been lifted as it would be by the constraint of fire or through an incision; and if it is like this, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not corrected, the body might still recover through medicine on its own or if the medicine takes effect, until your organs are even and your eyes in position; then place damp cotton with butter where the fire has burned, until your ears are numb, after treating the wound from ointment called 'dyafenis' and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to protect your work by great caution so that no medicine leaks into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes moist and the hair pricks in the eye, then reapply the medicine to that part of your head which has been softened by the clean paper, just as you did before; after treating it until it is healed. This is like the form of a parsley leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans vary greatly in size and smallness, and according to this apply your restraints; and do not let the right way be answered by him who studies this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Regarding the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the sections of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary for you to perform cauterization according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your proper care; cut the hair on their head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or remove their head; afterwards, apply damp cotton inside an egg or garlic juice to the eye; afterwards, heat the cauterizing instrument which is prepared: and be next to the head as if of a feather from a rooster's wing, place the cauterizer there; if you see that it points from one feather edge to another, and if you see that it is also like a tent; but all the same, it must stay in place for the sake of your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it has been opened, and treat the putrefaction, and dry it off; and if it is sealed, do the work, and remove from under the eyelid; afterwards place something hot on the cauterizer in a shape form, hold your hand at the cauterizing instrument near the part behind the ear above the eye, so that your hands do not go astray; and put the cauterizer into the grease of the oil, and let it be corrupted.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start the cautery again once more, and if needed elsewhere, leave it for three days; afterwards, place moist cotton on butter, and apply the ointment remover until it is dry, when it isn't, then put on corrosive water medicine until the bone is uncovered; and follow the instructions as they would come in their chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing fistulas that none of the old ones mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand about fistulas and make it clear; after that, place in the incision a thin stick of whatever is shown here:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And it should be the size of about three parts of lead; and hold your hand or camel firmly, and do not let the patient move, so that the melted lead does not drip into their eye; and when you place lead on the eye, use wet cotton dipped in egg whites or vinegar: the lead serves to treat the fistula, and it heals miraculously with great health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through cauterization as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer to the child, and to bring the fistula back into the body according to what suits its own natural place.
des crevaices en levres	Of cuts in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, there occur cuts in the lips which are called "whiskers", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cuts as we have instructed with divisions, and if the treatment does not benefit, then use .i. small surgical tool according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place them quickly into those wounds until they grow just a bit; after that, cleanse the wound of pus while it is still healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess arises in the root of the throat or in the lymph nodes, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotten and swelled up and become diseased and turned into a fistula; and you treat it as we have instructed in sections, and it does not improve: then it is necessary for you to have one cauterizing instrument according to the size of the fistula; afterwards remove the pus or foulness from the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron reaches the bottom of it, and even beyond. And do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, while it is still healthy; and if it can be treated like this, it's good; and if not, you should expose the wound and remove the decayed bone, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and this does not work, then place the head of the patient in their health; afterwards heat up the cautery as will be done later in this manner that you put a twig on the tooth; and place inside the cautery a small flame, and hold your hand so that the disease feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and apply it for an hour and then remove it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth which was moving is now fixed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the moisture has been eradicated and dried.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes due to coldness, or there is coldness or inflammation, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it must use the method of cautery according to two ways: and the butter cautery and the fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery if it is so that you take butter from a cow, and the tip in a spoon made of iron or copper; after taking cotton and wrap on the point of a tent, and moisten with the heated butter, then place it over the painful tooth quickly and hold until it has cooled; and do this often until its strength reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see wet wool and cotton in the cold butter, then put it over the painful tooth again, and heat one iron for as long as the fire goes into the tooth pain.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Use a fire cautery if that's what you desire, with something like an iron or lead tool, and make it large enough that the heat doesn't reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, from which it will form thus afterwards, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be relieved that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with plenty of butter in anticipation for this heat from the cautery, and then pull it out force; this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery of whatever size you desire, and according to your capability; this is the form of the cautery:
des scrophules	Regarding the treatment of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are of blood and cold moisture, and do not obey to digestion through medicines, then warm the cautery as described below to create its form. And make two openings for the fumes to escape from at the other side; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice according to necessity, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery in proportion to the size of the abscess, and leave it like this for three days. And put moistened cotton with butter over it until the pus is removed; afterwards cure by applications and dressing until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture invades the channels of the lungs, especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary for the patient to be treated first with diuretic medicines; after that, make the cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to go all the way up to the throat, but just a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After this, I performed another cautery at the joint of the neck on the spine's head, and use the cautery which is called "clavile", after which we have a model before us; treat the area as previously mentioned until it has healed.
de la toust	To the cautery of fire, command the sick person to let their hair grow long and evenly; and if they prick at their base when young, hold the eyes still so they do not move until they grow.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	For all illnesses related to the womb are due to cold moist conditions, and the patients do not have fever or dryness, they're an old illness. de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Regarding the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And each time it is set on this one nerve because there are seven cauterizations here.

Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture has been eliminated from the patient's body.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	For when colds and dampness affect the stomach to such an extent that they are in harmony with its constitution, causing multiple cases of purging, adopting common methods for treatment does not yield any benefits. And if you see it being cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach following this form; and whoever fears this cautery, cauterize by pressing and commanding it on the stomach at one point according to the amount that you see of it. Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the procedure we have undertaken, as long as it remains clean.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	Concerning the liver, which experiences pain due to coldness, moisture, and heavy wind. As long as it is weakened by excess through its natural disposition; and the illness is treated according to what we have said in divisions, but if it does not benefit from that, then it is necessary for the illness to be soothed on the liver's surface; and apply three marks of cauterization according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, below the lower ribs, where the pain originates; and leave a space between each mark the size of two fingers; and have the marks running along the length of the body, and do not press your hand too much across the entire area; and only let the inner half of the flesh be burned, and make the ill person lie correctly on his hands; and if he cannot, then lay down, extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is how it should be:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these fire cauteries with a knife, be subtle and wise in the art, and watch that you do not burn all the area, for you would dry up all the body; and do not let it boil over to the point of burning, because the areas are very subtle there, and you should know how to see.

When it has infected the liver, and you want to know if it's within the liver tissue or in the peritoneum: If it's within the tissue, you will feel a moderate pain; and if it's in the peritoneum, you'll feel intense pain.

Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois. dou cautere de pleuresin	of the weeping cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The old ones said that one should make weeping cauteries from the roots of aristological plant, and here's how: take a long root of aristological plant, the longest you can find, ensure it is dry, and also as thick and as long as your thumb; and soak it in oil, then place it on fire, and cauterize one cautery between the arm pit and the neck, and two smaller ones somewhat downwards on the part under the beard; and two more cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, slightly behind; and one around the navel, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and four more along both sides of the hip below the cautery which is between the two shoulders; and do not squeeze your hand, just apply it as you would smell it.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And it was said by every old one that no man uses the fire cautery at the rash, and heats it up and puts it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess; and when it escapes, the pain goes away, as we have stated about the gallbladder abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this chapter there is fear or death comes to those who now die, or a fistula occurs that cannot be cured.
de la mice	Of mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin. de ydropisie	Of cautery by fire, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not suitable for lead poisoning, except in the way that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat according to the methods we have discussed in sections, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary for you to make four cauterizations around the anus, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one under the kidneys, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place below the navel. And let the cauteries be well near the spinal bone of the pelvis.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After allowing the cauterization to remain open for a long time due to pus formation, and do not cease the treatment on the disease after the cauterization; and healing would hasten, and both the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is that which we have shown before; and the one for the back is olibanaceous, according to what was set out previously.

de la hainche	From the hip

And Dioscorides states that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with the dung of goats, if assistance is not much needed; and the cauterizations should be done in this manner.
