Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking the dung of dry goats, heat it until it turns to charcoal, and place it on wool, letting it remain until it is extinguished; repeat this process again, without stopping until you think it has come up to the hips, and that the pain has ceased. This method of cauterization is called "goat dung cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or impact, or too much evacuation, or through exposure to cold matter, none of these conditions warrant cauterization, for it is akin to that which arises from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After ensuring that the patient's body is free of foul pills or other similar symptoms, one should apply treatments to the back, at the site where the pain resides, three lines marked with a cross, and in each line up to five cauterizations depending on how much and how intensely the body can endure; perform the cauterization using the cauterization method known as "points"; and if you see fit, do three or four cauterizations halfway between the cauterization for the clavicle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often affects small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they seem pale when they stand up, and fear; you find it in the last spinal cord at the back and we see the appearance coming on other spinal cords.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe its treatment,
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If one uses a proper fire cautery for each segment of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, apply the fire cautery along the spine at the point where it pierces two lines or three, and have the points close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treatment until it is healed according to what we have said, and be cautious not to apply the fire cautery in locations that are near nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture that spreads throughout the body, and when pain comes in the foot, they call it "gout" properly, and when it's caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicine, it should be treated using cauteries in this manner: make a fire cautery inside the joint of the foot, and let the cautery use olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you touch on the back of the foot, if it needs cautery across the whole cautery mark, which we claim as "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains extend up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if you need to apply cautery on each knee for three or four cauterizations per part, all along the olive-shaped mark; and if you need more, do so as needed, but don't let your hand stray until the skin burns.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knees and behind the back, then apply the cautery as we have described in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points between the fingers two lines; and if there remains any pain on the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to elbows or up to shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if you treat him well and purge his humors, may he be cured with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture in the kidney
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes about in the lungs, and the bowels descend to the kidneys, this is newly happening. It's necessary that when you look at them being cured, they don't eat anything during that day; and they should use things that lighten the stomach, so that the wind descends from their belly. After have them sit up on their back between your hands, then command him to cut his arm until the intestines are repaired, and bring it back with your fingers, and feel for under the rupture upon the bone of the wrist, and do all at a sign as if it were half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery that is described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and discharges pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the boils at their root; and instruct your attendants to pinch his hand so they don't turn around; and operate well on the thighs for the patient, and place one sponge and one surgeon on each thigh, and another under his buttocks that pinches his hands; then apply the cautery to every sign across your whole hand, and hold it straight until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again a few more times as long as you can reach the bone; and watch carefully so that the boil does not escape when you use the cautery; don't burn them; and by this means patients may die or suffer other ailments.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach up to the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be delicate according to their size, and for large people also big in proportion to theirs; after three days cleanse the wound with butter until the scab is removed; afterwards apply other dressings until it heals properly, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well; and ensure these treatments last long enough so that pus does not leak when he wishes to move about in chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, have a well-made bandage ready for him and keep it on for another forty days. And ensure good rest, that he works little and avoids overeating or drinking too much, and doesn't strain himself excessively; and if he follows this advice, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after this chapter on the treatment of surgery.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	And when wounds occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then I will do the cautery as much as needed according to its quantity, and let it be red hot at one-third of the rod; after treating it according to what we have said; and none of the old ones have said that one should cauterize with the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain occurs in any limb, or due to falling or being hit, and if this pain lasts long, and medicine does not cure it, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "points", and the cauterizations should follow the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its utility and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cautery application, that's good; if not, apply another cautery to this one, because these tools are such that they should heat the limb that is nearby, so you must perform the cautery until the patient recovers.
de meselerie	In mixture
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases are aided once by each application of the cautery and similarly, the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of blood and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see the cauterizer? Take care that the disease is at the beginning, and if it's cured according to what we've said in the division, and doesn't recur nor remain, then you doubt if corruption spreads throughout the body. So perform two cauterizations on the head: I heat the front of the head to the nose, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II over the two horns, and I behind on the jawbone; and let your hand be so that the cauterizer goes until the bone, and as long as the scales come out so that the vapors of the thick fluids can escape; and cauterize the neck accordingly to what it appears.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is everywhere spread out and it's clearly apparent, then it's necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries that we've mentioned on the head and one cautery in the middle of the nose, and two cauteries on the spine from the neck to the back, and six on the spine from the shoulder blades down, and one large on the knee and another slightly smaller, and two on each shoulder blade; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn any nerves that are under the back part of the heel, do not burn them. And never cauterize near the bone in the elbow, and another one near the bone of the stomach, and one near the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more often I apply the cautery, the greater help I provide and the more benefit it yields; and be aware that patients do not feel pain from the cautery as healthy individuals would, because their bodies are already thoroughly corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the size of the cautery be large or small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find in the methods of iron tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, wash the area with flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it is clean.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation occurs in any limb and is treated with medicine, oils, and bandages but remains infected, then apply cautery to the limb according to its size or smallness; and let the cautery penetrate somewhat into the site of the sore; then treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no matter where you make a cautery and at the hand and on the foot and back, in the area of the nerve that makes the limb move, then this is when the swelling occurs; and always do not interfere with it unless one knows about limbs and the exits of moving nerves within the body.
de albaras	Of cauteries by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes still so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has worsened, and medical remedies are of no use, then use a small cautery to cauterize, according to the size of the lesion, until the pus is removed and its color changes; then cleanse with flour mixed with lentils, rose oil, and plantain leaves, as well as blood from colognes and almond birds, each in their part. Mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, apply it to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of gangrene by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When gangrene begins, and you see it start to stop, if you apply the cautery at the spot that seems like a circle, all around the perimeter of the gangrene.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And still, some wise people say that one should apply the cautery in the middle of the gangrene; and yet this does not seem right to me, for fear it might lead to further erosion and corruption, which is something I have already decided not to do again. And a more appropriate approach would be to apply the cautery all around, at the spot that's referred to as 'circular', just like we have explained in another context about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot die.

When someone has an illness that is called 'adubelati', and it prolongs death or causes it due to overactivity or the aging of the body when it becomes old (meaning too old), and there's little blood, or due to tension; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize internally with several small cauteries by touching them; afterwards leave it like that.

li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire using a iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else but a member abscess, as it corrodes the limbs like dry wood.

des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From stones that come into joints
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Sometimes it happens that stones that emerge from the body cause a disease called "cyst" according to our understanding, and it's a large lump that causes pain in the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterizations for this disease can be done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	The fire cautery if you heat it, and the hot iron cautery is like a feather from a goose. Make it of good iron at the size that it can grasp nails in all directions, and ensure it has sharp margins; after this, place it fully heated on the nail, and turn your hand around entirely until the heat goes to the tip of the nail; then leave it like this for three days until pus begins to form; afterwards make a poultice from powdered wild garlic mixed with oil, and leave the poultice overnight. The nail will fall out and be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with a thick ointment until it becomes clean.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are inverted through the belly of the body, and it happens many times in hands and feet, then you should bring this hot cautery to them; and do it thus: take a spider's leg or iron rod, or a goose feather pen, and place them on a nail and an apple, meaning for warts; and place the rod so that it burns everything around it completely. Then add a bit of hot water, hold your hand well, press your hand as the edge of the rod turns to the root of the nail, then find the path of hot water deeply until it reaches the root; and let the patient endure for an hour the burning sensation from the hot water; then leave them like this, and they will be eradicated from all their roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Continue in this manner with each one, until you have treated all those located on the body, then cleanse of any growths that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from cold or nerves, or from intermittent fever or otherwise, it is necessary that you apply three or four hot water cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one near the elbow, and one under the stomach with an olive oil cautery. If this continues to cause shaking, then hasten their recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	of the pus-filled sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	When it becomes visible through openings on the surface of the body, or pus-filled ulcers that come from large decomposed matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	When it becomes visible that one should apply a cautery to each head of the pustule: a fine wooden stick from myrtle wood with its tip held over fire or a long root of aristolochia plant, or use a lens-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time should they cauterize until they become visible in this manner, and it cannot grow into further concerns, but the excess that causes it is eliminated, making them well; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery has been tied
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there have been great flows of blood from the artery that has been tied at the wound, or during an incision on an abscess, or during the cauterization of a limb, and similar incidents; it is very distressing to smell this.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless, when this happens to any part of the body, if you rush to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, hold it there until the skin becomes calm under your finger and no more drop flows; then heat several olive oil cauteries, both large and small, until they are all red. Then take one (or according to the size), larger or smaller depending on the wound and where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, keep the cautery there until the skin becomes cool again.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are heated, take quickly one more of the cauteries that are hot.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the skin becomes cool; and watch that you don't burn the nerve underneath it, and that no harm comes to the patient; and know that when the skin is cut off from the artery, one can hardly properly cool it themselves when the artery is large, unless it's through one of the four methods we have mentioned: by cautery, or extraction if it wasn't treated yet, or with strong string application, or by applying medicine that has the power to cool blood; and tie and hold in place for future use.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer treatment by tightly binding with cloths or by placing burning objects thereupon, or other similar things, if it doesn't benefit then do not proceed.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no sight or medicine at hand, if they must apply their index finger onto the wound of the vein as we said earlier, stretch it well so that it remains stuck under the wound and under the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often until it is very cold. And create gaps in front of those who need cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases where it is necessary to apply a fire cautery or medicine that is heated, and we discussed their uses, causes, instruments, and forms. We ended that chapter on the topic of burns until the skin, and I will continue with this chapter using the same approach for those who find them easier to understand and need them.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this, it is fitting for you, dear apprentice, to understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first use of the cautery, and for this reason greater caution should be taken.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often blood evacuation when opening veins, and incisions on abscesses, and treatments for wounds, and extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar operations; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to embark on foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come to treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who were so afflicted by their illness that they died slightly due to the fearfulness they found in their sickness, and from the severity of their malady; and one must have fear about this.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these it gives its meaning, and says: "Wait, I am sick"; and the illness is vexing.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It would not be right for you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but give more caution to your honor than to your covetousness, and do not open blindly but wisely to what you are certain of and can take and leave; and use prediction and guidance in treating the illnesses of whom health has been converted; and this will help you gain good reputation, glory, and long-lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe the holy inspiration of their hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or let me have ordered this chapter in devising by chapters, according to which is before or the chapter of cauterizations, that I have devised from the head until the foot, so you will find it more easily when you need it.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes about very often in infants at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the baby's head; and sometimes it happens due to no other reason than we don't know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never see this disease outside of infants, and among all those that I have seen their death hastened; and for this reason it seems to me worth abandoning the practice of such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of this, where the shoulder was full of water, and their head swelled each day until it could no longer be supported; and because of so much moisture he died, and this moisture is assembled around the bone under the elbow, between the chest and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is within the chest and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you make a large cut across the head; and let it be as long as two hands, as long as the moisture runs; and see this form of spasm:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	When moisture accumulates more, and if the abscess is bigger, make two incisions in a manner like a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if moisture is under the bone, and you see the corners of the forehead opening on each side, and a sharp pain occurs when you press it from your hand internally, and this does not respond: then it must be that you cut through the center of the forehead with three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all moisture completely outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After restraining the cuts from cloths and powders, and I place wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head remain restrained equally, and eventually have the patient consume dry meat of a little moist until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the aperture of the abscess opens, and the assembly of the water; for it never stands in front; nor behind; nor to the right; and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut the place where the abscess opens and the water filling it, make a cut according to your ability and watch that you do not cut the artery; look for a source of blood, so that the patient dies from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	regarding remedies
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any illness that is called "catarrh" either around the eyes or at the bottom of the nose, and this sickness is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort treatment involves cauterization using what one would cut off their two main arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	So then, if you see fit, the patient must be freed after their head; after rubbing their face with a hard cloth until the arteries can be seen, then pull out the ears' necks to all the cloth; then look where the veins lie, and both sides are compared after the ears, and they have returned; then sign the sides with an incision, then cleanse each side with a sharp spatula of two parts, until the edge reaches the bone, and this is done considering the width under the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see this, hold the knife over the artery and cut above it, making the incision also as wide as two inches through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, make sure to pull the string continuously upwards from there.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open by touch, then you must measure the size of the space to be three fingers wide, and gently apply pressure until it reaches the bone; and what needs to come out through blood is six c/ (a unit of measurement), and in case a little more or less depending on how well the patient can endure it and fullness of the artery; then inspect the wound: if it remains over the bone near the sinus, and if an incision does not show when removing pus, then tighten the wound and bandage, and apply ointment treatment until it heals.
de emigrainne	Of grains
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old age comes along and severe colds occur, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and elsewhere, as well as similar conditions. Medicine is treated through the methods of medicinal cures, but none of these help it much. Then we extract the veins in the temples and cauterize them, just like what we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for their extraction is that one should lead the patient's hair from the temples to where the artery opens on them, as it opens well by its pulsation and responds only in those whose heads are overly cold; and if it does respond, hold the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rub the head with a rough cloth, and raise the head under hot water until the artery clearly appears; then take out the cautery tool that has this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly strip the skin until you feel the artery, then pinch it upwards with forceps, and remove well all the membranes that are under each part; and if the artery is delicate, then turn it at the tip of the nail, then clip off that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, neither does it jump all through all without pain.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain out the blood until the seventh day; and if the artery is large, it's necessary that you tie it with two strands of a sturdy silk thread, so that putrefaction doesn't occur before the healing of the wound, or during bleeding; then cut away any excess material between the two threads at this very moment. And when you see fit, apply cautery from the surgical knife until the bone, as long as the bones are cut. This is the main task, should the patient not have fever and their complexion be warm.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizers are help to finish the moisture: because with them it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	It is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the whole with old cotton and place well-made tents above it; and when they are released, if you do a cure with dry medicines that generate pus and tents until it becomes clear; and if there's no artery bleeding then do as you work, quickly apply heat from the cauterizer, or use the whole of vitriol and squeeze it in your hand so that the blood becomes congealed; and if you don't have this on hand, fill the hand with alcohol until the blood is frozen, and dip the hand in cold water until the bleeding stops, then hold it as needed; and what is softer and more fluid during the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein from this cauterized trenching at .ij. parts, but the trenching should be well spaced to keep heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tense, they retain less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives half an inch, and then when you have decided to insert both of them, and you place the heated iron until it reaches the bone, and cut along two lines; and keep them far apart as this cautery does not fully adhere everywhere; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are draining through the veins that are under the skin of the head and face, and no benefit comes from medicine being applied there, you'll see the skin turn red, and feel or notice heat on the forehead as if it were pulsating; and at such places they become damp and wet so that paper hairs fall off, and the papers get heated, and are burnt by the heat of the tears, in which case this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And call the old "blister cure", and if you treat the patient with this disease, make them grow hairs on their head or forehead, then I make three cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; let one cut be as long as two thirds of the front area moving forward to the nose tip and keep the rest at lengths equal to half of the front in both sides above the eyebrows. Be careful not to cut through the arteries located above the eyebrows; maintain distance from the continuation of the lower jaw bones, and each wound should be about three inches wide across. Have a piece of sponge and some cloths ready for wiping off blood, then start with the hot pincers from two sides as depicted here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut that is behind the temple until the second cut; and remove all the flesh in between the two cuts up to the part on the bone, then continue with another cut from the middle cut until the other second one, and then remove this spit.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you use the tool called "cultellaire" in the first opening, and it is very sharp on one side, and blunt on the other, not sharp, and this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And make the cut towards the fatty tissue under the skin, and the cut meets the bone at the corner, and the knife reaches to the middle of the slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the veins coming down from the head until you reach an opening at the corner, and then continue the incision halfway through the slit; and after that perform equal bleeding and express the wound from the blood taken; then place a piece of old cotton in each slit, and cover with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and sage, making sure no pus comes out; and on the third day remove the bandages, and apply large amounts of water, then administer a cure with basil oil and rose oil, as well as other treatments used for wounds until they heal.
dou reume des eulz	from the inflammation
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to sudden fever and habituated coughing, and you see the eyes red and small, and weakening of vision, and burned paper; and hair falls out, and one sweats profusely, and the body aches with malaria-like pains, and the patient shivers; then know through these incidents that those matters and this fever come from many veins, and the treatment given, if it is such.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you must instruct the patient to rest their forehead, then make a large cut in the middle of the forehead, and another one below it that is about an inch wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Start from the temple on the left to the temple on the right and make your incision until you reach the bone; keep your hand away from the temples' nerves that move during eating. When the bone is revealed, drain all the blood with a sponge and then clean between the two lips of the incision, place old cotton and linen strips. Then cover it with wet bandages in wine and oil. Avoid any pus. Once the bone is removed, you should rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then use desiccating substances that stimulate cartilage growth.

des poilz des papieres	The phrase "des poilz des papieres" translates to "the hairs of paper". This could refer to thin or lightweight material that resembles hair, possibly used in various crafts or as a decorative element.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in unnatural places on the body, and they become thick, they can harm the eyes and cause issues leading to diseases like frequent tearing of the eye and inflammation or swelling of the paper-like layers under the skin as well as albugine (a condition affecting the eye). All this happens due to damage to the eyes. The cure for such conditions involves three methods: using a cautery device combined with fire, applying an ague medicine according to what is described in the section about cauteries, or performing incisions and suturing, depending on how I explain later.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz. puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cover that which is on top with small force evenly according to the shape which is here:
