And when the tooth has been pulled, wash the wound with wine or brandy and vinegar; and if bleeding occurs (which is common), apply vinegar to the wound; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, to which one binds their teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large parts that do not bend while being pulled, and be made of well-crafted iron, and have teeth for holding things in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays during bleeding, it is necessary that you place cotton soaked in greasy butter under the wound for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the legs are softened, take and hold the tongs known as "algiefri", which make the surgeon's cut seem like a beak; and they should be done inside in such a way that it resembles a file, this is its form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these clamps, then it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh right up to the root, and place the tool called 'althali', which is known as a palainche, as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps over this, it's good; if not, use all your tools, as those mentioned next will come into play:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you assist with the tool having two points, as described here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools located in front according to their place, and from this tool that seems like a pair of large tongs, as depicted here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this one of your tools so that it may not break, and know that there are many types of dense tools; also other tools, which are not counted among the rest; and the wise masters themselves discover their own tool by themselves, according to what their work and disease reveal to them. For there are certain diseases where the old did not teach a tool because of the diversity in these ones, and if it breaks due to wear or from other bones, or if it decays, when they seek out the tools that suit them, that I have told you about, and aid with gestures, as what follows is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well held to hold the bone, so that it doesn't escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore him to the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you use all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and its shape is ugly, especially even in virgins, you must know if this tooth was born after another tooth, and it isn't placed straight, and one can neither file nor saw it: so you should remove it; and if it's next to a tooth, take this instrument that has the following form, and resembles two small beaks, and it is made of hard iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the dentist holds the molar tooth gently and very firmly with their hands for its hardness of the tooth surface, and because you do not move the others, and if it is visible that one can shave it off, then he shaves it with half of a file in this way:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And also like the file used to make needles; and he files the tooth gently in his hands softly, so that it does not move until it grinds; then makes the flat part at the end using all kinds of raspers, and if its edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must file down the roughness until it is even, so as not to hurt the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth before the cavity, or by percussion or impact, and when the patient cannot press on what they eat that they do not defecate, and you have cured them with medicines that restrict it; and this does not work; then it is necessary to restrain them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and choose threads neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see to straighten the teeth, take the thread and the double pinch between two healthy teeth, then place the cuttings between the diseased teeth, as long as you can do so until you reach a healthy tooth from another side; then repeat the covering up to the part where you stopped, and gently pull your hand, until it does not move at all; and tie your knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the teeth with thread on tweezers, and join them together, setting them between a healthy tooth and its socket; then place it so that it does not irritate the tongue; and leave it like this as narrow as possible, should it move or come loose, in which case use another thread to secure it. This keeps it usable for all of its time, forming the shape of the teeth and the placement of the two healthy second molars, just as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, you put it back in its place, step by step, as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't appropriate or tolerable, and never form the shape of an ox's bone tooth, and put it in the place where there is a defect, and hold it just like we've said, and remains and serves for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the tongue wound
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time should the thread come from under the tongue or nature, for that is how we are born; or through accidental welding in a wound; and the operations are such that you work on the mouth around the disease, having its head in your healthy place, and lift the tongue; then take out this nervous thread as wide as possible while the tongue is detached from its place. If there's hardness or clotting, which might be due to sudden injury, if you break the hook and cut it wider instead. And remember that the incision should not be too far off-center since there is an artery underneath; when done, lift your head with a rose-colored mildness or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue each night so the teeth cannot weld.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding should come about, place sulfur on the wound; and if it doesn't stop bleeding, apply the slow-acting cautery; this is good for that sort of thing. Then treat with other remedies until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the ailment has turned to red or black or hard so that the patient doesn't feel it, do not touch it because it's gangrene; and should it turn from yellow to green and there be moisture, then pinch the hook and drain a thin pus, and cleanse from both sides; and if the wound discharges when you don't apply anything, pour vinegar on top until it is cleaned out, then return to your work until all strength has been applied; after that place the head in cool water and steam, and proceed with other treatments until they have healed fully.
des apostemes de la gorge	From throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No infection enters the throat cavities which are called 'godath', and they are properly named the II almonds. When you treat them as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, then take care: If these are hard abscesses with a small sense of touch and a reddish color, do not even touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron for blood leakage; but leave it until it is reduced, then you will remove it or it would break on its own. And if it's of a white color and the root is fine, prepare your instrument to cover, but first check if the abscess has cooled down and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	So make the sick person sit in front of the sun, and have them hold their hands out to you healthy. Let them open their mouth and have your assistant grasp their wrists between their hands, pressing the tongue down completely onto every instrument; this is how it should be done; also use finely made silver or small sharp tools like knives for this task.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this tool, and see if there's pus? Take the onion and the point of the almond, pull it up more than you can; and don't remove anything from the threads with it. Then scoop it out with the tool; this is how it looks like a force; and every spot that was affected, one place then another, they're very sharp, and made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool now, take the scissors; this is how it looks like:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make an incision on one side and the other; and when you have completed one of the almonds, complete the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot, cold water, or cold and gentle water. If bleeding occurs during this process, then continue to gargle with hot water, or use cooked currant fruits, or rosemary leaves, or similar substances until the wound is healed; then complete the cure when it is healthy; and if any other abscesses form in the throat besides the two almonds, you should remove them accordingly like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is known as the small abscess; and had blocked off almost the entire throat very well, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and could not eat or drink, and died if she had continued in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had to be drained twice, once through each nostril of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I acted quickly then, inserting one into the anus. The other was pulled out, and a large amount of feces came with it. Then I did another operation on the remaining part near the nose, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, inserted the onion into the abscesses, took away some parts, only a little blood came out; in this way, the throat was removed from the woman, she began to drink water and then wine immediately after that; I did not stop cutting the abscess for a long time; the abscesses grew back right away, filling up the place I had emptied, as much as it could be filled until it became quite large; then I fastened it and cauterized inside her throat: in this way, she stopped growing. Then I moved on to these parts, and God did something good for her after me.
de l’uve	Regarding the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the sperm descends to the uterus, and it inflates and becomes lengthy, it is called 'perpendicular'. And if it is off-side large and spherical, it is called 'ovum'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure doesn't help, and you notice that the extraction wound has calmed down, and it is subtle; so you should take it. And the one which is round gathered and isn't lengthy; and it is bloody or of a reddish color or black, so you should avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So, when you see it, according to the method that I have said, of its smell and length, you should make the patient stand in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the tool that we described before; then insert the spoon into the ovum, pull it outwards, and take it using the two instruments I mentioned during the incision of the two almond-shaped organs.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut beyond the natural limit of excess; for if you cut more than this, damage will occur to the voice and speech. And after making an incision, use what we have advised about incisions in two amonds, and treat until healing has occurred.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patients have fear about cutting, it is necessary that you use something from the cautery for the sense of pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is like boiling water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patients direct their head towards your health, and then press the tongue with the tool we said or chapter of cautery, rubbing vigorously with hot water, ensuring it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the movement of this tool, as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put our head with some hair on which we apply the medicine, just like the movements of a spoon, and place the tool over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus go from their mouth inside to the medicine, ensuring it doesn't descend into the throat or the stomach; then hold your hand with the medicine and press onto the eye for half an hour's quantity until you see its numbness and the medicine's impacts have calmed; if you notice, take cotton and wrap it in any tool, soak it with medicine, insert that tool inside the cotton all the way to the string, until the cotton dries on the eye; repeat this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and close afterwards for 4 days or 5. If you need to restart the medicine's cautery, do so, and after the cautery cleanse around the eye with gauze soaked in butter, clean up what is inside of the medicine; rinse from cold water, and wash with gargling until it heals fully.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or with the cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile and hyssop and rosemary and rue and calendula and parsley and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them into one pot, then place it there, and bring to a boil; and ensure that the pot is well filled with strong earth, and within the pot there be two sticks as this method dictates:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it be made of silver or arsenic, and whether one places the other shoulder in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead; after that you often repeat this process, until the eye dries out, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the coming of pus, because many things occur; also do not perform this when the pus is receding.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a piece of wood and place an eggshell in the patient's mouth, so that the hotness does not burn too much the maimed; because the eggshell does not let the vapor damage the mouth, and it is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there is air in the throat bone or spine of fish, without any issue; therefore, it's necessary that you remove what you can see, and press the tongue at noon to all the tool, so that you can see if something moves; and if this doesn't reveal anything and remains in the throat, it's fitting that you make the patient vomit until the illness is expelled; by chance if the illness is pushed out through vomiting. Or if the illness swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one chunk of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it again; and when she comes to the head, if she is expelled by air, and then pull out forcefully; and if this doesn't work as described, take one tool of a plonc according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer. li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses

de squinance	The text "de squinance" refers to issues related to or conditions caused by malalignment or misplacement, which is a common theme in medieval medical texts dealing with anatomy and orthopedics. It could refer to deformities, dislocations, or other types of misalignments that affect parts of the body such as joints or bones.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke of the surgery to alter the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and that is written from their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting vision, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called 'epiglottis' be avoided; and one should not take help from this, because all the veins and the heart are at risk for those who have a foreign body in their mouth, or in the throat or between two gums.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the channel of the heart, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It follows, when we wish to incise the epiglottis, that we make an incision through three or four small cuts across it, between the two circles, or by the quantity of the cut within them, not in the cartilage. And this is advantageous for sectioning the epiglottis as there is no meat, and the vessel is long from beginning to end.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extends the throat skin to almost all of it, then incise the keur until it reaches the thymus; and avoid blood vessels, if you see anything at all, and then cut through the syphuncle as we have said; this has been demonstrated by the jump of the flow from the thymus due to the breakdown of the organ, and by the loss of voice; leave the wound open for a bit.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed since one doubts strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound neatly, and all along the skin until the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim asserts that one should not perform this until the throat is entirely swollen, and the patient's organs are judged dead, and the defect has been made.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	So care must be taken with the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe properly and is breathing through their wound. This prevents them from dying and this is what the ancient healers advised: to keep the wound open as long as the disease's harmful effects have passed, and they have indeed passed after three days or four. And then they were instructed to stitch up the wound and treat it until it was healed; and I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I witnessed that a maiden took the knife and stabbed herself in her neck, cutting some of the veins near the heart; and I was summoned to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I saw well that there had been no opened vein or outlet but rather the windpipe, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed, dressed the wound, and treated her until she was healed; she only suffered from hoarseness and returned to her usual self afterwards; for this reason, I say that when tailoring (cutting) the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	The text refers to the removal of abscesses, often called "throat hernia", which is a large abscess with color like a raisin, and is very common among women. There are two kinds: natural or accidental; natural does not have any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And accidents occur in two ways, with one seeming like fatness and the other resembling an abscess coming from our arteries. There is fear, it doesn't allow to make fire outside until it's small, and one must thoroughly examine all parts: if you find it alike to what we're used to, if it cannot reach any vein, then cut it out, just like you'd cut fat tissue, pull it out with all its covering, if there is any; and search well around it, treat it accordingly until it's completely cured.
des nous	from the mouse
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways exist for us, so I will mention all similarities; now it is necessary that I explain the entire difference between us and the outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is marked by heat and fever until the boiling has passed and decay been completed; thus the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new, there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains pus, which is its own sac and lies within the body's color, starts off like a lump, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, oily or moist, and most colors are as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new wound, that you first test and inquire about every tool which is called 'entrainer', according to its shape or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiring about pus in us is that you squeeze it more moist than you find inside the abscess, and twist your thumbs little by little, until you know that the instruments have penetrated deeply, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the pus, and be careful not to jump force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture corrodes the wound, no matter what color it is, if it cuts as I said about other abscesses; and if after the incision there's still no moisture, you know it's fatty, then cut straight across, and take hold of it with tweezers, and gently scrape each side and keep the bandage where the wound lies that you pull out the cloth soundly with the stitch. And if you can't pull it out soundly, remove in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, the illness returns by many times; and if some does remain, but it doesn't bother you, fill the wound with corrosive water-based powders, hold the wound in place, and apply warm abscess-soothing things, and treat other treatments until it's clean; and if the illness is large, cut both sides of the wound, and treat the one that festers pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too large or goes against the grain and rushes you, tie off the wound, and use the lead of vitriol in small portions, and let it sit for two days or three, as long as the wound heals from within, then rest with a bloodletting; afterwards return to your usual treatment.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of embolae instruments and they exist in three ways: large, medium, and small. And there are three types that are called 'albaret', one is called 'breb'. There are also three sizes for these: large, medium, and small, to encompass abscesses from fistulas. They resemble sewing needles which surgeons use on wounds, made of amethyst, iron, or silver. Yellow ones are considered valuable and those with black cork are better suited for enclosing the turns in fistulas. There are three forms: large, medium, and small according to the width of the cuts needed.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the forceps resemble these, as you see here: large, medium, and small. There are also forceps with two turns in three different ways; there are those with three turns and they too come in three forms; some have two turns each, and there are single-turn forceps, all coming in three forms; all of this is necessary by their type.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this person is sharpened for surgery, and there are those who do not cut by force from one side only; they sear the skin because with them one does not sever the vein or nerve. And these penetrators have their blades in cuffs, so that the patient does not notice during abscess opening; and there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and none of them cuts by force only in meaty parts such as legs, arms, nipples, ribs, and similar areas; and on no occasion is another small instrument used, resembling gynecological scalpels according to this form, with which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once at its natural location in the body, near veins and arteries, and never according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	None of the male breasts swell up when they begin to be corrupted, resembling female breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them should do so according to this form from this line .b. until .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and apply medicine to the wound. Then join the two sides of the wound together with stitches, performing a cure until it heals completely; if there is an excess on the nipple when it hangs downwards due to its size like in women, cut it into two parts above it, by two similar slashes; from where one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, up to the line .b. until to the line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two sides and remove the fat, and apply as we have instructed about stitches and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it heals completely; if it has not healed or if the incision is not fully done, because the patient doesn't want to rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with moist cotton wool in a corrosive ointment; then leave it until it begins to heal and replaces both the cloth and fat. Then cure it until it fully heals.
des apostemes des asselles	removing abscesses from the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that occur in the armpits are methods of hard scrofula or those with knots, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should have their limbs cut according to this shape, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat with ointment as long as it is clean.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble scrophula sores, cut them as we have said in cuts for scrophula sores, and if the wound is full of pus, apply a cautery as we have said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	regarding the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin sewn above it, many times there are discharges; and this also happens with veins and abscesses. And if one knows that it's because of the artery, then these discharges tend to be long and full; and when you feel constriction with your fingers, you sense this tension; and when it is about a vein, it becomes obvious in its cut surface; and this is foolishness to treat this discharge like so, and likewise if it occurs on sides and angles, and around the neck, or in other various places, and being very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid iron treatment, and one should also avoid it on the head. For the one inflated by artery, make cuts above the skin as long as possible; then work along the inches, cut out the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a tool underneath, and pierce up to the other side, and bind the artery with double thread according to what I have taught you in extracting two arteries that are in temples. Then remove the tissue between the two links of an introducer until liquid comes out completely, and relieve the discharge; then apply treatment that stops bleeding, until the link bleeds; and treat this with ointment as long as it is clean. And if the discharge comes through the artery, you should dye your hand where you touch the discharge to the whole skin, then insert a needle under the tissue that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and have double thread, so that you pull from the other side; then tie the discharge as I have told you, or tie one part of two from both sides with thread; and if you doubt whether the thread will pass, then reinsert another needle under all the discharge at the first incision site, and bind the threads in four. Then cut off the excess until it bleeds out, then cut off this extra skin according to your technique and leave what is tied. Then apply a damp pad of wine and oil, then continue treatments with bandages and ointments as long as it heals.
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as with abscesses in the artery and vein, there are nerve abscesses when they are inflamed, or due to too much work, and similar conditions.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and everywhere there are joints. This is the state of an abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and can be seen in various positions with no pain; and when it's compressed, the patient feels pain, but not within the body, but beneath the skin; and moves all over the place, neither advancing nor retreating, neither upwards nor downwards, and the one who is suffering from joint issues should never cover them with iron: by chance, there might be a contraction; and the one who has it on the head or forehead, makes the scalp taut.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, take them out with your tweezers by pinching them at their base; and if they're large, hold onto them near the elbow, cut them open, then peel away some skin, expose the bone, and stitch up the wound. Continue the treatment until it heals properly.
des grosses boces pendans	of large breasts hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never occurs in the womb or anywhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its appearance, and has a subtle root, and large heads; and there are small ones as well as many very big ones. I have seen two people with bellies that resemble fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference between them, they were white, had small roots, were split down the middle, and corroded inside due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found that one was eighteen ounces in weight, and the other six. The operations during incision are such that when you look at it, the disease appears moist, and the color of the inner body is white and moist with a subtle root; if you catch it under the large spot, and see the fire cautery being held before your eyes.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when surgeons come, there are often too many bloodlettings, and if they fail, then you should quickly use a cautery; and if you see that the patient is frightened by the incision from the iron, then take a well-made cotton thread, tie it at the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then hold it, not stopping to tighten the cotton thread until it touches the joint, doing everything without effort; and if the roots are large, they feel fearful when touching their own stomachs, but you can only properly touch half of them, then cauterize so that they do not swell again; then treat the wound, and ensure that you do not touch the thread which has a red color, little feeling, and is milky.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When it comes to the eye,
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	When it comes to the buboes it arises from the wound cautery or the tear of the syphilis, and is on the belly and there are some of the glands, as it happens in other ulcers, or blood that leaks from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned previously, or due to windiness; and if this is through the syphilis tear and the exit of the pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and there is little feeling, no pain, and opens up from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it's due to the output of the intestine, then it's more varied. When you press it with your fingers, it goes back up and then comes down again. Sometimes it gets stuck and swells significantly when entering hot water and due to hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it's a simple matter, and opens well when you press with your hand, not restraining at all; and if it's due to blood, it opens by these signs large and hard abscesses, implanted according to quantity; and if it's due to winds, it stings in the finger, and the veins such that when you look its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or vein, or winds.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you let the treatment proceed.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
