des maladies de la vessie	Illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled, and you see distilled waters and medicines there, then make for all the instrument which is called 'clepsydra', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and if there are three parts: two from one side and one from the other, as you can see; and the legs come through in such a way that medicine should be such that it numbs well the penis without addition, if only moisture can be treated, and drive out when necessary; and when you see your medicines flowing into the bladder, put the head of the needle into the moisture, and guide to the one who is pulling; if pull out the moisture at the needle, and then re-bone strongly the one being pulled afterwards; so that moisture enters in this way, comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of a subtle cyst where you catheterize the bladder: and here it goes:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or iron, and the shoulder is higher up; and just above the first breast or where the nipples are. Then take a sheep bladder and put in the moisture that you want to catheterize the bladder with, then place this piece between the two breasts forming a good double thread, and heat one end of the thread on fire; then put the head of the catheter in the penis, then pull your hand over the bladder until all the moisture is gone, so that the patient feels it has arrived at the bladder. And if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, and poke a hole through it neatly; then tie this piece firmly into these three parts with thread, then assemble the circle as you would assemble a doughnut, and put inside what you see from urine, moisture, and water, and bind in the tool. Do this as if you were making a bladder, pressing with your hand until all the moisture goes to the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have discussed the methods for stone division and extraction together with medicine; and we explained the differences between stones in the kidneys and all their signs, and when to operate on a kidney stone; and also about the bladder and the penis; and I will clearly and briefly explain this to you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I state that stones that occur in the bladder often happen to children, and this is a sign that there is an obstruction of the bladder similar to the obstruction found within it; one should open the bladder canal and cleanse the patient's penis several times, then apply a bandage; and after many of these obstructions they find their way down. And it takes gentle healing for infants until they are around four years old, it causes much distress in the elderly, and occurs moderately among those in middle age, between childhood and old age; and it is easier to treat those with larger stones than those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with purging, in order to remove all the bile that is within the body.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often clogs when trying to cut into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the ribs, and lift them up and move them backward, so that the stone descends to the front of the bladder, and does not come out from his upper body; then make him sit between your hands prepared for operation, and let his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is fully sloped downwards; then press and touch inside; if you feel the stone in space, now hurry to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she doesn't poop at the toucher all around, moisten your index finger of your left hand with oil from the palm of your hand, if the patient is young or your middle finger, if the patient is a young adult; and press it on his back, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, lift it to the neck of the bladder; then press at your finger, and cut behind where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the surgeon to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards above the genitals, and have his left hand hold the skin that is over the genitals in the part where the cut is made; then he pulls out the urethra smoothly, which looks like this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And place the one who is between the shoulders and the foundation, not midway but at the side of the left snow; make it straight on the stone, and let your hands touch or rest on the foundation, and have its size through the middle so that it may be broad outwardly and narrow inwardly, according to the size of the stone, not too large; if by chance there is a press against the hand which rests on the foundation, it might jump out without effort; and know that there are parts of the stone with angles and edges: it gets hurt when trying to emerge; and if in some part it is beneath, resembling a nut, and round, where its exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	Then at the part which has angles and edges, make the size bigger; and if it does not jump out, you must tighten with the tongs that are as sharp as a file to force the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you push down on this small, curved fine tool; and if you can't work like this, you widen it a bit more than the tip of your thumb, and if you remove it smoothly, then force with vitriol; and if there are several stones, first break the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut upwards, then pull strongly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then she needs to be removed, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For there are two things that happen to the patient: or they die, or their urine begins coming out immediately when their legs cannot be sewn together; but all the same try to drain or fragment with tweezers as long as you can remove it piece by piece. And once you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, then compress it, and place oil and wine or oil and rose water and cold water on top of the cloth to soothe the inflamed area; then bandage the patient around their neck and do not untie the tie until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, make sure to dry and clean the area very well, then apply an ointment of laudanum and a balsamic ointment until it heals properly.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses fester in the wound and corrosion occurs, or blood clots in the bladder, causing retention of urine as it would without urination: then you must clean the wound and remove that blood, because if it remains, it will decay the bladder and cause damage. Then cleanse the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in every way you can until he recovers; and you should bind his two thighs together, and place medicines on his legs whenever you treat him.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it comes from where the penis goes in, and is stuck there, so urine cannot come out; when you treat this as I say, that you cut many times, and let part of the cutting go for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already gained this experience like this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron tree according to this shape and have it pierced with three pegs on one prong.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis near the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder. Then cut in the penis gently until you reach the stone; and push the needle in the penis slightly, until you reach the stone; and turn the needle in your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; if urine starts coming soon, then press your hand on what is stuck of the stone which is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is suddenly broken, and there's a rush with the urine, and the skin scratches the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie one thread over the stone and the other above, then make the passage between the two threads through the stone, pull forcefully, remove the thread, cleanse the clot of blood that is in the wound; and treat until it becomes clean.
de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone becomes enmeshed in women, and if it occurs once, then the treatment is difficult, and forbidden for three reasons: one is perhaps that the woman is virginal; and the second reason is that we cannot find a woman who knows how to protect herself from looking at men, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third method is that by chance one cannot find a woman who well understands this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone in a woman's body is more centrally placed than the stone in a man, so it requires deeper surgery, which causes much fear. And if necessity forces you to do this, you should seek out an experienced person and place their finger where yours would be, and if you cannot find one, choose some other tool; and present her with good knowledge of the female anatomy, or a woman who understands part of this art, and command that she follow your instructions for extracting the stone; and examine very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then you must press her elbow or foundation point and search for the stone; and when she finds it, force her to press on her elbow or beneath the skin with her left hand tightly, and squeeze her hand against her stomach firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it steadily from the entrance of the bladder until below, while it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the knee, where small bones emerge and you feel the bone in that area; and do not move her hand above or below the bone, keep your fingers very close; first make a small incision; then force out the kidney through this incision as long as it can come out forcefully, knowing many types of stones exist: these are that they are small and large, hard and soft, sharp and smooth, long and round, with some having grooves.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you understand the symptoms to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it doesn't harm him, put sulfur on the wound for an hour until the pain subsides. Then return to your work until the stone is hard and use the tools I've told you about in extracting stones so they can help you with your task; and if the pain doesn't subside, and what's cut off is an artery, apply powder to the wound and pressure dressings and bandages, and don't repeat this process again. Leave the stone alone and don't remove it for fear that the patient might die from it. Then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of blood has been calmed, and the wounds have healed, then return to your task, as long as the stone remains intact.
de hernie carnouse	regarding fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Glandular watery substance is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white pus, which is found within the skin of the testicles that contains an egg; and it's called "pus", and it's never properly in the membrane of the egg if one thinks there could be another kind; and this is the skin under the testicle where we have said the white pus lies; and this doesn't have a pore.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of such glandular matter is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this substance spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does such come from percussion on the kidneys, and this moisture takes many colors: or it becomes a declining yellow color, or there is without redness, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are signs to recognize this condition, because if it is or white pale as we have said, then pus forms, I do not mean as long as the figure of an egg, and does not open up the kidneys, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if he has moisture in the proper membrane, then pus forms with part of the egg, and because this is believed to be another egg; and if there is moisture between the skin of the kidney and the pale white, you perceive it well; therefore when you know the color of the moisture, you test everything within the square, as shown before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	So according to what comes after penetration, judge on this one that is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to our strength and the replenishment of his body; then sit on his back, at one place somewhat high, and set cloth underneath him. Then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, stretch out the leg to one of his two ribs near where the knee is; then take the iron rod, cut through the skin among it long until under the knife, make sure the cut is all straight going diagonally up from cutting the skin until reaching white flesh, and gently scrape off subtly according to our strength; then pierce the white flesh fully with water until quite deep, extract all the water, and then put in your stitches, stretching out that area upwards; do not touch the ribs, but only let the white flesh alone. Cut everything or piece by piece carefully along his side where it's delicate, if you don't cut it properly it will return to being wet; and if an egg starts jumping during your work, reset it into its place when you have completed the work at that spot; then stitch together the two flaps near the ribs onto one seam, then treat as other wounds until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit. Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the knife is assembled into two parts together, know that these are two branches; then handle the other part as you did with the first equally, afterward evacuate the blood, and place wetted wool in the wound drenched in rose oil; and place another layer of damp wool in vinegar and oil, and place this on both sides, and cover it with double cloths, and secure it all around following this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take II cloths and fold them into wool rags according to this pattern and sew them together in the waistband of trousers, and one of the shoulder blades hangs down to the belly until the back, and the other is on the part below the elbow; and another pair of chief above both joints, and everything must be assembled with the tightening of the garter; and each time you treat this branch of cautery with a metal rod instead of a metal tool, and that you take the second small cautery tool subtilly, then cut the skin around the joints, and heat it as we have said until the white substance in the water is exposed; then take the cautery according to this shape, and puncture the pus sac through the oncines, and burn it with this sharp cautery chaut:

No silver paste or copper paste is ever made, or melted spider or wax; and no small or large instrument is ever made according to the one it's being applied to.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when dealing with the treatment of children and those who are weak and in pain, they need small things.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small or large paste is like this, or the stomachs are bound in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if the belly is tied and pierced in the middle, as you see, and the head is completely pierced; and there are two holes on one side and one on the other; and fill the belly with medicine from a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce it all around with small holes. There should be an inch of space between each hole, then insert in these holes a strong thread twisted into a braid for ten inches or so, and sew up the belly like a goat. And when the medicine is inside, tie it before with a strong thread, then catheterize; this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and smear the head with oil or yolk of egg balm, or similar thing, then gently put it out. Then the surgeons guide their two hands together until all is visible; then remove the cyst, and lift up the patient's legs to the bed, and if the medicine is meant to come out, pull it out as much as you can; and if he sleeps through a whole night, this provides more significant help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer castor oil for the ailment of belly evacuation, and the medicine is meant to quickly come out, then repeat it until he feels better.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the bleeding is from a vessel or an ulcer, then even if the cyst is as delicate as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate cyst where the skin is compressed:
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have discussed the treatment of wounds in the section on healing; now we will discuss hand care and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are varied depending on how they are made, and where they are made in the body, and why they were caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The causes of wounds are by penetration of bone, size of a sword or knife edge, or spear or bow shaft or ax, or similar objects; or those made according to the parts of the body, such as a bite on the neck, head, stomach, or belly, or liver and other bodily members; and I will tell you how to treat each wound, starting with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I state that when a simple wound or head injury occurs and the bone is not broken, you must be careful whether it is caused by stone or similar things. Even though the skin has been completely torn apart and the wound is large, if you slightly doubt there being pus, do this: if there's a small amount of blood coming from the wound, then immediately cleanse with the surgical technique for the head in the same manner; and if not, instead clean it against the removed part. Make the patient intoxicated with wine and rich meats afterwards to help replenish their body.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't want to be treated with surgery, reduce its meat intake, don't drink wine and avoid eating any meat. Apply a substance on the wound, should pus appear, use cotton soaked in oil or rose water; and if there's no pus present, apply on the fresh bloodied wound, as long as it hasn't been disturbed by air, use a powder I will mention shortly; and if it has become disturbed by air, apply some remedies until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a tailor's cut and similar injuries, and the lips cannot be joined together by stitching, then join them through sewing, as I will say for wounds in the belly, with stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes the bone, it heals only for a little while if held; then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh instead of skin. Instruct the patient to consume large meats like testicles and cooked wheat or corn, as well as things alike.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or discover a rotten skin and it does not reach the bone, then cut out the rot completely, let it bleed, and then treat it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, where it is torn off, and it cannot be stopped with medicine, then pull out the artery, and if you find that it's dislocated, hold it in place with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you put this powder which seals in such a way that when the fire touches it, it stops moving.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of fresh charcoal, and finely powdered. Apply this to the wound, pack it firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, leave it undisturbed if it does not swell; for you do not remove the medicine until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do this with charcoal alone, when one doesn't have the incense or the dragon's blood oil, but only that the surgeon has treated the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heart has healed the wound, equally in state, then do not put this powder there at all; but apply some digested ointments, or oats flour soaked in water and honey, as long as it produces exudation. Then continue with other treatments until it is well.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone breakage comes with the wound and it is small, then use delicate tweezers to extract it; and I will tell you about bone breaks in the head later.
de la plaie dou col	from the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound occurs in the neck and is simple, if there's no difference between this and those of the head, but if it affects the throat or the artery, then that makes a difference.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, just leave the treatment alone and don't put anything restrictive on them because it harms the nerves and causes them to withdraw; don't place anything cold on the wound either, as nerve substance is cold and it continues with the head which is one of the highest body parts; but use a mild medicine like watered-down soap or mixed with rose oil, and watered-down cucumber, and other minerals done this way, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it with bandages as long as it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with blood, then you should penetrate or go further down than usual. And if there's an artery cut, and bleeding ensues from that, you must open it up, repair it, and cauterize as needed; and if the phlegm of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the guiding pathway kept, where food travels, you should place the windpipe above the base of the throat without touching it but adjust according to its natural shape; then restrain for some days after that, let it heal from drying out until it's well; and if the wound made an impression in the bone, you should remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, you must take them all out thoroughly or leave any that can't be removed, allowing the wound to heal completely and be discharged by its own means; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder as I have mentioned on top of the powder.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has an abscess, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from the wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, if you look at how the air jumps in the wound against the body: then know that the wound is fatal. And if it's not deep, and it's fresh up to its blood, don't put any powder there on the first hour, nor tie anything there due to the blood not flowing out fully and returning to the heart, and making the patient idle; but instead apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, then insert old cotton in the wound for absorbing moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days or four or more; if there are no convulsions nor tremors from the heart, then it won't strain anymore against itself. But when you see good conditions, and know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it therefore with various remedies and other treatments as long as the wound is clean. And if she cannot heal or work, realize that there may be a fistula; do treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision and it's simple or worse on the back, the treatment should depend on whether the person who is in charge performs it. If it's large, treat with stitches; and if it's small, use powder. If it's deep into the bone and has pieces of bones that need to be removed, determine how to treat the wound based on that. If they are not exposed, let the wound heal by itself or ease out the extractions; and for other wounds on other parts of the body, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The abdominal operations are large, medium-sized, and small. Large wounds may cause the intestines or parts of the intestines to protrude due to the introduction of foreign objects; and stitching is more difficult. None of the small wounds are worse than larger ones because when we put back the intestines several times through the hole if they were not replaced gradually, as it's common with large wounds, since the intestines swell soon upon feeling cold if they don't go in properly. Therefore, a smaller wound is better; for this reason, you should reinsert the intestine to its normal position as we'll discuss each method and explain further.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no part of the intestine is involved, or if there's a need to remove something damaged, this can be done through one of two methods: either by taking advantage of the size of the wound as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it's cold, heat the patient in this manner: soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in water alone, or cook it with boiling water and vinegar and thyme, then raise the intestines until the swelling is drained; and do not let the drink settle to help reduce inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water or broth that has been cooked well, for this helps to reduce the entrance of little things; and if it doesn't enter, make a small cut in the wound near where stitches are removed. And the first cure should be done until the cut is healed before any further cutting is made unless there's great necessity; and these are the tools for making cuts: you cut inside around the curve and outward not, and this is how it looks:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are expelled, if you can set it back according to its natural form in its proper place, do so, because that's what matters.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is extensive, and it's located in the abdominal area, you should make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it's below the abdomen, place the head and buttocks higher than the abdominal parts; similarly, when there is a rupture in the abdomen, if it's in one of the two halves, you should position yourself so that the affected part is higher than the other. And thus, how I have said to manage large and medium wounds should be followed.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have at hand. Then take the holy scalpel and cut through all parts of the wound with it; stitch together the edges; this is a common way to suture, and when using needles, choose ones that are neither too fine nor too thick. Start by leaving two finger-widths from the edge of the wound and insert a needle or multiple needles depending on the width of the wound, then leave one finger-width at the beginning of the wound and insert the needle with strong thread; pierce both parts of the skin through the layers of fat until you reach the layer under the skin. Tie together the two ends of the fat tissue in three groups; then stitch tightly by threading the threads back and forth between these parts, leaving one finger-width apart for each stitch and inserting another needle. Sew as you did with the first needle following your need for needles, until all the wound is stitched up. Use needles that are neither too fine nor too thick since thin needles cut through the flesh well while thick ones may not fit properly; do not push the needles too far into the flesh or skin risk of further tearing in front of the stitches; and when you have finished suturing, tie off the ends of the needles to prevent them from irritating the patient during sleep. Place a bandage over the needle points for insulation until the wound has healed; this stitching technique is more suitable for small wounds because it involves using one needle twice before performing the second stitch which is common and includes sewing together both parts of the skin and fat tissue in one needle with medium thread. After making these four stitches, draw the needle back to where you started as if you were sewing a cloth. Leave an inch between each stitch for width; this method heals effectively and I successfully sutured a wound on someone who had been stabbed through the abdomen, which was torn open by a knife, with the wound being over a palm wide and containing intestines thick like two palms, and it was a wound in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place then let it rest for 24 hours, and the wound healed up until the 15th day. I treated it, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when the sight told them he was going to die, it became a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in the region where no such thing could be found, nor any medicine; instead, I laid cotton bandages on his wound twice a day, washing it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and place it from the outside part up to the inside; when it has pierced the body straight in and out, then hold the needle at the opening or where you have stitched, and make another hole from the inside part up to the outside. And the idea behind this stitching is that you stitch as a squirrel would sew fur, leaving an incision on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the entire stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen properly described, is as follows: no one does it like this. They join the two parts together naturally and apply one needle's point to the other part's point. Here is how it should be done: thread a needle or needle's point from nearby, pierce only that side, then leave both parts of the stitch alone; next turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside just up until where there are stitches on each side; then pierce one and the other from the outside all the way to the inside, using two more needles' points which are at another part. This is the usual and most correct method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said these words and no one attests to them: that we should stitch the belly with two needles, or have thread in each; and must one sew a needle from one side and another from the other, like those who stitch corroies; and know that when the tear is within the belly, this stitching is more painful than the others' around their belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments concerning the wound are such as those for other wounds: and that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, just like when the surgeon has cleaned it out, you replace the intestine and skin. Then apply some absorbing powder on top; and if the surgeon has done this cleaning, apply no ointment until the wound heals; continue treating until the wound closes. Sew up any torn threads, ensure proper stitches for the suture, and care for the suture site; then treat the wound like others, until it is healed. And should you lack medicines, as soon as it begins to heal properly, use old cotton, and agitate this twice a day until it heals completely.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For if you need no other medicine for simple wounds; and should there be doubt that the wound is spreading to main limbs, it's proper to apply a thin layer of oiled linen or linseed oil, or in boiled heat oil, on all joints, and inside at the elbow creases; and when there feels to be pain or gangrene developing several times, it's appropriate to perform an enema with black wine, and similarly if gangrene reaches as far as the intestines; then pierce internally, and know that when this refers to large intestine, it heals more easily than small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called 'young' cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and its approach towards the nerves in its nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the hair leaps out of the wound, then put it back in the same way as the intestine when it is fresh. And if it is old and turned to brown or black, then you should tie up what is black so that no blood flows, for there are veins and arteries; then cut out what is between the tie, and hang both ends under part of the wound up to beyond it in order to facilitate extraction when the hair falls out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and there's a small wound, one can attempt to restore it in various ways. I observed that once someone was pierced by a spear or sword, and there was a wound on the right side of the stomach; it became inflamed and turned into a fistula where food waste and gas could escape. I treated it according to my understanding and persisted with refinement until it was healed, then sewed up the edges.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it fused together, I wondered if the patient might have pain in their abdomen; there was no harm but stayed better off, ate and drank; and many experimentors said that when they have a small injury in the intestine, it should be tied in this way: take large fir cones, then join the edges of the wound, and once the fir cone has opened its mouth, place it between the two edges, if she presses her mouth against them; then press down on the cone, making sure it cannot slip off, then place another fir cone in the same manner as before until the entire wound is covered; by this method, the wound heals.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	In the case where something clogs in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a delicate thread cut from an animal's intestine, done like this: take the tip of the intestine thread that is well deshucked, then wind it around the tip of this intestinal thread along with some thin linen thread, tie them together into a needle, sew the intestine using this method, and pull back in the seam; this way of sewing thorns follows the path of faith and hope. And if the wound is large and wide, especially when located on one of the colon's regions, it will not cause obstruction or harm because of its delicacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	regarding a fistula or if it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, as it matures, is universally called a "fistula", and even when it is hairy and turns red.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodulation firm and white, where no pain is felt, and it is also hairy like feathers of a bird; and sometimes with clear redness, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times sufficiently so; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every unhealed wound, as long as there's no pus, can only discharge externally through one of the eight causes: namely, due to slight bleeding or ulcers; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard pus within and on the membranes, which does not allow pus to be produced; or there is too much pus; or the veins are swollen, and the material has a bad quality; or the medicine used in treatment was ineffective; or because of how pestilence spreads; or because digestion is slow in that region, causing delayed recovery, and pushed by nature; or if there are vessels or bones involved: and I have already shown these causes, along with their signs, and treatments for medicines in this division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of fistulas which is performed by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas exist in all body parts; because there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, either at the heart or within the intestines, or bladder, or certain areas of the back, or on any joint of hands or feet; and if it happens to affect the function of the main body part, and affects their semblance.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are this way are painful in healing, and there is nothing else but labor and ignorance; and if any fistula doesn't come up to where I have mentioned, and you've completed its treatment, and recognize it, then take an arachnid web or a metal wire, if the fistula is straight, follow it; and if the fistula is bent, seek out a subtle needle tool, for the ants bend their body along the tortuous path; and if the fistula has missing parts and you can't properly search by tools, then flush it through one of its missing parts, as moisture travels from one part to another and cleans. Then search it carefully with your strength, so you understand whether there is bone or nerve inside, and that it's full filled throughout; ask well the patient about their pain when pressed with your hand, and where they feel it; and once you truly know where it is, and if it isn't near a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the parts I mentioned, then cut according to what I've said, remove the pus-filled parts inside; and treat until it's healed. If the fistula was deeply cut straight, so must you cut until properly reaching there, then place wet cloths in medicine as a cure, and apply them up to the tip of the fistula, until the medicine eats away the excess that's remained at the bottom; then apply fresh healthy flesh for healing, until it is healed. If it isn't healed by this means, cauterize if we have said so before, and if the bone has been corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves are not blocked or main limbs suffer thus as we have said; and if bones are exposed, and there is decay and darkness, cure until all decay has been removed, then cleanse the affected flesh until it heals naturally; and if it does not heal naturally, follow the same procedure as before. Realize you have not yet reached completion: continue to expose and clean until you reach the bottom, removing every bit of decay; then restore the limb; and if it is thus healed, it's correct.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, realize that the decay is too advanced for removal. Let nature handle it if there's no other option. If there are small corrupted bones, you can pull them with forceps if possible or use a suitable tool and extract each one, without leaving any behind. And if moisture hinders this process, causing no fear or danger, work on the bone structure along with the moisture and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something stimulating for putrefaction on the wound, and leave it until the hairs inside are completely rotten in relation to the bone. Then they will come off more easily; and if it's a large bone like from the leg or thigh, only let the corruption go as long as the black part is entirely removed, then repair the wound; and if there's a significant portion of corruption going up to the bone, you should remove and cover all until the corruption ends, then treat until it heals; and I will tell you about an occurrence in a person's leg that involved this.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something originating inside the body that spread until it reached the leg. A large abscess formed and there was no reason for opening; but doctors operated on him extensively, resulting in the abscesses being opened and causing them to eat away at much tissue, forming a fistula, and it led to great loss of bodily fluids and moisture from the body; and many doctors treated this for two years without any knowledge in medical practice until I was called, saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him, and the corrosion through the losses with significant internal damage; and the body would become red like youth again, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent on one of these bumps, and then searched all the bumps, finding that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurriedly worked on one of the bumps and found a part of the bone within it. Then I began again, uncovering the bone as before, only to find that the corruption had continued within the bone itself.
