It healed quickly and without any complications. There was no need to repeat the procedure besides due to the patient's weakness from sickness, which could not bear it, and because of my fear of death that I had concerning this case.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often, during bloodletting, it was completely healed. In the place of the bone came a hard flesh, and it had good quality without causing harm or opposition from all sides, neither inside nor outside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, should be treated as follows: take hold of it, and stretch at the end of the bone that opens up, commanding to stretch it upwards; then tie another thicker thread than the first one, and tie it over the flesh that's inside the bone, stretching the edge so that you can pull out the rotten flesh from below, revealing the clean flesh on the wound where you want to heal. Make sure not to harm or touch the clean flesh. Place a poker or a board under the bone to cover the rotten flesh; and treat as much as one can see and feel the corruption, then treat again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and doesn't open, and the corruption lies in middle or a part, then reveal all flesh; afterwards place a hot rod thereupon, and then let heat travel from one part to another of the corruption, and let the heat last as long as necessary on any part, just as we have said; and if the corruption is within the joint, then cut into the corrupted joint and heat the bone where it lies elsewhere; and if the corruption lies in the continuity of two joints, then there's no angle other than to cut across them; and if the corruption lies under a finger of the hand or foot, this thing will be very strong indeed but still, you should inquire how this corrosion appears to you; and clean everything out using all the methods that are useful, but without harming either the vein or nerve; know that the incision blade and instruments for operating on bones vary according to the nature of the bone, appearance of its surface, size, fineness, length and smallness, hardness; and thus it suits you to equip yourself with every kind of tool for each kind of work based upon your knowledge in this art, and testimony from various diseases; so consider what instrument you need as suited according to its nature.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints swell either from within or from outside; and when you have tried to heal this corrosion through medicine treatment, but it doesn't improve, then one must cover that limb up until the point of corrosion comes, so that the disease escapes by the body dying, or by malevolence, which is greater than the fault in the limb; and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they have been burned with fire, and after the blackness, because the corruption spreads from member to member, taking over the whole body; so you must hurry to cover it, and if it's caused by the beating of certain poisonous beasts, such as sea scorpion and snake etc., then if the corrosion is in the head of the spine, then treat it, and don't give it space to come up until the hand.

And if it comes up to the hand, when you treat the joint, so that the corrosion doesn't go up to the elbow; and if it goes to the elbow, when you cut in at the wrist; and if it passes the wrist, then it's death, and there's no cure beyond the quantity of its virtue; and do this way whenever the corrosion comes or if it has spread: If it comes in the first joint, when you treat after the other joint; and if it spreads, then treat throughout the area where it has spread; and if it goes up to the leg, then treat at the joint of the knee; and if it gets above the knee, there's no other way than to let the patient die; and the method of treating or securing the limb is that you bind over and under, stretching one pair of bandages down from below and another pair going up from above, and you cut out the flesh between the two bands as wide as possible until bone is exposed; then treat or secure it, and place a linen wrap on each side so that the wrap doesn't touch the healthy part, causing further injury to the patient.

de la voinne civile	from the civil gum

Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein show themselves such that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then change your limbs, and the vein begins to emerge outside, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder joint opens, it must be covered with a piece of linen from two thirds to three-quarters and up to ten pieces. You wrap and tie it around the limb, leaving the linen hanging down to the leg, and each time if there is any remaining, you cover again inside the linen, tying it; and if it's too long, cut off some part and wrap again, ensuring not to cover its root until it's fully out; otherwise, if you cover it, it gets inside the muscle, brings pus or decay at the site, causing bad disease. Since this thing must be treated little by little up to there, leave nothing behind in the process, and only once this vein is treated to a length of five palm widths or ten palms, and slightly more than twenty days when it comes out from ten palm widths long, then when you cover it, it's necessary for you to have left over one inch or two inches and pierce till bottom, so that everything goes out; let the inner matter be emptied, apply purging medicine once a day until it heals as with pus.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein by manual pressure, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or at the foot, there is a lot of loss, and it hurts to touch; so then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "cattle disease", because it affects cattle, and there are small worms that grow between the skin and flesh, and travel throughout the body going up and down. One can feel discomfort as the disease progresses from part to part of the body until it reaches the skin where it causes an irritation or outbreak; and it is accompanied by pus from various bodily fluids, such as coming towards and resembling snakes, worms and roundworms or those in the stomach; there's doubt about its severity because when it travels through the body and goes up to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one can only say when it is going: hence you must then tie the arm up above and below with a very tight firm string, then pull upwards and drain it outwards, and if it is moving within the flesh, and you do not find it, then you burn it with fire until it stops; and the greater nuisances that it causes, if they go towards the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or its head near to the eye, then firmly tie over it the eyelid folds, then pull upwards, and drain it outwards; and you must use the aid of purification through remedies' bodily fluids for the maladies produced by humors, and be cautious with raw meat causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to any limbs, and then moves from one limb to another; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to tend a patient with a malady, and upon examining her arms, I noticed a small swelling in the veins of one arm. Soon after, I observed it ascend even like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything else, just as liquid silver when cut from one place to another; the pain left that place and settled into the shoulder, then shortly afterward spread throughout the entire body until it reached the other arm; then she would tell me that it was moving internally within her body, just like I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how she moved from member to member in this manner, for I had never seen this disease like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	In all cases, I desired to move the pain from one place to another, but it did not happen like this for me, just as what I observed in that woman; and I thought that it was because she had a dry body, with exposed veins, and due to this restriction of air pressure; they cannot be seen according to this reasoning in those who are delicious (i.e., those who have moist bodies and their vessels replete).
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then press on it quickly from above downwards, and then hold for as long as that windiness is constrained in its place; and apply a cautery to it; and if you do not see it at your eyes, treat the one who deboutes the windiness, as with fetid pills, pill of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, depending on their shape and where they pierce the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety lies in this that there are those with large points, and small ones, and tailed ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those which have tongues, and those where it has pieces; and the one that excretes in no member as it excretes in any manner: or in a primary limb, such as head, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it is dislocated then in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death which I will tell you later on becomes apparent: you should proceed with the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in various conditions; and when that bad sign does not become apparent, or the arrow has not been fully removed, then you should remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow penetrates through to bone and jumps over the head which is on top of the brain, it's when blindness and deafness occur together with vertigo, reddening and heat in eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion, vomiting of bile; and sometimes loss of strength in the nostrils or ears; and sometimes loss of speech and voice; and a wet white rash around the wound that looks like pus, and also as if burned; and when this sign becomes apparent, then you should take it seriously and remove the arrow if it's there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of pregnancy when she is at ease or in her heart, indicates that she is near the left breast and feels as if something has been driven into a hard thing, not empty; and by chance the ovum also stops like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never comes out is when there's no foam escaping from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient has a changed complexion, and breathes loudly and feels cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow exits through the armpit area, it is located beneath the ribs; and there's copious bleeding and intense pain, with labored breathing; and all limbs move freely from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach is stuck, by chance something from the undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach is stuck in the chest or abdomen, and nothing comes out through the intestines, there's no hope for treatment, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow or stomach penetrates into the bladder, and urine comes out in spurts and exits, causing great pain to the patient: you should know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other parts of the body, such as the limbs (including arms and legs), neck, throat, shoulder blades, shoulders, shoulder girdle, back spine, ribs, and buttocks, along with any similar limb, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the muscle or artery, and it isn't poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you did this other thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow hit him in the thigh at the root of his nose: I tested it and pulled it out from the other side through the fat behind the ear, it came out cleanly without much trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I pulled out an arrow for a game that had hit in the fat behind the eye close to the paper, and the arrow was retracted, yet only its tip could be reached towards the shaft, and the arrow was big as a Turkish bow, all the iron was clean without any ears; the player was fine, and he did not experience any bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pull out an arrow from the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arabian arrow in the ears: I pulled it as far as possible while holding my breath, and made sure to remove all parts of it, leaving no trace on the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from the home, that was stuck in either chest or abdomen, and thought he would die; but after having passed 30 days, his condition did not change at all; I cut into the arrow, pried it free, and pulled it out, with no bad incident occurring.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a home with an arrow that has fallen onto or into it, and the wound is healed inside; and the arrow remains within, not altering its natural disposition, nor causing harm in any of its natural actions.

And observe this other man, who was hit in the face by an arrow and had his wound sewn up; and he endured suffering from great pain afterwards; and many were similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And one arrow hit the king's home of princes, piercing his nose and causing him to tilt slightly towards the right side; and the arrow was completely stuck. I was called for treatment after it had pierced for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it with all my skill, but could not feel it; and he felt pain and discomfort in his right ear.

I thought it might be the tip of the arrow. I placed an adhesive and digestive plaster on his nose because his ears were not swelling up; and I saw the arrow's tip in his ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days and resolved the wound immediately. Then I let the patient remain in pain for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose on the third day; and I told him this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed corrosive ague medicine on the wound for several days until it was opened and then tried it. I felt the tip of the arrow which was near the bone; then adjusted within the wound opening with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent. It took about four months well into the termination, and then I freed the wound so that the healing was obvious from both sides, but could not remove it entirely; thus continued refining and engineering ways to make instruments until on the third day I grasped it with well-made forceps as shown in the final part of this chapter, then pulled it out and allowed the wound to heal.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors decide that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I will do so then, and after sealing the wound, the patient would be completely well.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I've told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so please apply your skills to what I don't explain here; as books can't capture everything. But wise colleagues compare well for a bit of significant knowledge, and for the current situation and its shortcomings, find nine new works, and nine new tools, in the elimination of occurrences that happen within this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I state that arrows enter the limbs where they are inserted based on two ways: either through the body or where they penetrate, or from another side; and when it enters or penetrates there, this is an arrow entering into the flesh, and now never happens.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it until the ulcer is completely healed internally, and the discharge has stopped; and similarly, if it's embedded in bone and can't come out, leave it like that for a few days, removing some each day; then it will jump. If it doesn't jump, puncture inside all through the fine hole as long as the flesh internally is broadened, and then remove it afterwards.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow is embedded in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the glands under the brain, or any other accidents I have mentioned to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but let it until it becomes even after a few days; for when the arrow reaches this far, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire. Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is placed back in its original position inside your body where you can't see it, and you try to pull it out with all your might; and if you feel it, trying to pull it using any suitable tool; and if you cannot do so because of the constriction around the wound or due to the depth of the arrow, and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein inside, then cut as large as possible through the wound; pull out the arrow when you can, and if it has ears attached at the point it holds onto, remove any flesh stuck in two parts that will move, and then bend or break the ears off the arrow as much as you can while trying to pull it. Be sure not to damage the arrow during this process, so you could extract it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, let the shaft be broken up to where its fletching is, then try again, for the extraction should be done quickly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding deters you from what we have advised about treatment in this chapter, then heed our instructions; and guard against cutting the nerve and vein, and do it cautiously as you can draw out the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to their original shape when they had been struck by the arrow, for that is the best guide, if you cannot follow this, then position them according to what the symptoms show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from the other side, or if there is an opening in it, or if the skin is swollen at the spot so you can see or feel it obviously: then cut above, as long as the forceps might grasp, and then press: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around as long as it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, let her stay and start extracting again until she does come out; and if the arrow's tip is there, hold all of it; and if it's a piece from the arrow, when you see how to handle it correctly, then provide it with a tool that has hair, so that the arrow's point goes into the tool's hair; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is caught, when you apply force to the tool at the tip going in, making extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow touches the body, you must remove all tissue around where I come in, if possible, then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. des sainies de ventouse	of cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or spiders, or snakes; and suction therapy can be performed in two ways: by bleeding and drawing blood, or without causing bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which can cause injury is done in two ways: either immediately with no heat, or with heat; and the cupping that is done by causing injury and bleeding takes place on the twelfth ribs of the body, from which one is completely located above the head; and another is within the neck; and two others are on both sides of the neck; and the cup is placed under the chin; and the cup is placed over each shoulder; and the cup is applied to pimple areas; and the cups are placed around both arms; and the cups are placed on both legs; and the cups are placed under the ankles; and cupping does not target blood, for there are small veins that are scattered throughout the body flesh, and because of this they do not weaken in any way as in a blood treatment; and it should not be administered in any illness resulting from over-fullness until all parts of the body have been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.
