And guard the one who is being purified and is choleric, and if they are too hot and inflamed; it should be that they take cold things, such as apples, endives, lettuce, and similar items, and nibble on small fish, and meat from a castrated animal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should take honey syrup and a moderately scented wine, which is between old and new, as well as nibbling small portions and eating small fish and young birds and poults; on the day they are to be suctioned, they must drink more than eat; it is appropriate to give some men neither triamcinolone nor muscat before or after suction therapy for comfort of the main limbs; and make them wear a loin cloth, but it should not happen that anyone who is hot drinks.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Cauldrons that are used to cause harm are those placed on the liver, and on the kidneys, and in gout, and on the abdomen and the throat, and hips; because this part does not endure being harmed by heat, and it is done only for extracting blood from one part of the body to another. Just as we apply them on nipples when a child cries; for removing viscosity that exists within the limb; applying the suction cups on the abdomen and on the throat to diminish the size of limb; and removes pain whenever there's an obstruction or stone, and it accidentally removes the obstruction by its attractive power, or empties the stone from its place; and so does this when placed on liver and kidneys where there is retained viscosity; these suction cups are administered empty solely for sucking. They are never administered together with fire at all times, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of pleursin, and in such manner that we fill the suction cup with boiling water or hot water containing suitable herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup applied by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And take two fingers of half a palm in length, and place them about the middle inch inside, just like to push a needle through, both in front and behind so as not to hurt the patient when placing on the limb; and have an inch wide rod across from spiders or iron, for holding a candle waxed, with it being both large and small according to the diseases and condition of those who use them; for children's suckers are different from adults', and they differ in thin people than in fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup onto the limb like this: take the candle wax or the rod with a line, and insert it through the suction cup along the rod that's inside the suction cup, ensuring the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so as not to burn the patient; then put it on the limb, and hold your fingers above the part we've mentioned, so when you want to do it again, if there is vapor going out, remove the suction cup; and take the line similarly as before, and repeat often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction method therefore that is administered during childbirth distress, at all stages of fever, there should be neither a defect nor excess, and it should only be used when it is full of fluid, and placed solely on the body part; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without suction methods are used only for limbs where we cannot place suction devices due to their small size such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and for those who lack flesh in the armpits like elbows or knees, and other similar parts; and the quality of using it is that when you find slippery without any stickiness in mild water, take them; and put one in mild water until they become familiar and have nothing in their stomachs; and then cleanse with a vein and suction device, then rub the body part until it turns red, and place them on the suction parts; and when they are full and start to pull away, if there is a place where we can place a suction device, then do so, for this works very well afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it's not so, then lift the limb from the aid, and then from water, quite well, and then apply oil. And if the skin has healed too much after a long time, soak it in cold water with linen cloth until it becomes moist; and if there are many wounds, put powdered vitriol or garlic on them, until they become moist; or you may place half peeled bean skins over the wound, leave them until they dry out on the limb, then it will stop bleeding now; and if you need more, get other blades.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not heal quickly, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or you can stick a needle in until it draws blood, and place them there; soon after, as they smell the blood, they will start to dry; and when you see that they are expelling things, sprinkle some aloes and ground flour or ash over them, and they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoration of breaks and healing.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, child of the earth, that the people in this chapter are venturing into topics never found in ancient books or ever read from letters; and for this reason, the knowledge has been hidden in our land since I have never encountered anyone proficient. And as a result, I am ignorant of these matters, having studied them through the ancient books' science, which I practiced thoroughly enough to treat that science, also by experimenting and adapting to my way of life's routine; and in this chapter, I described what is contained here clearly and condensed it at the end, showing the forms of the instruments used so well as I did in the two chapters preceding these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or introduce the contents of this book with its principles and chapters where the mind accepts understanding, staying true to reality. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when any fracture or dislocation or twists or bruises occur in any limb, you must quickly cleanse the patient on both sides without causing harm if there's no obstacle such as weakness of limbs, children, old people; if the body is too thin, too cold, or too old; and avoid eating cold foods, such as chilled soups, eye and fennel; do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill up your stomach with meat that fills veins with blood until you have no doubt of pus formation in the limb or spreading of matter into the body; let the patient heal under their first governance which they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you introduce meats into the diet that cause substantial bloating or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and radishes, and onions, and peas, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And with this type of bloating, the healing occurs more quickly and the breakage improves.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in old or weak people cannot be healed or joined according to their nature due to the drying of limbs, nor those that are too tender, like baby's bones; but with care, fix them back onto the broken bone, the thick tendons which expand and unite the limb together, until it holds as it was before; and don't cut off from his work entirely, for this requires fattening up with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	Know that fractures can occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the heel or leg, and in this chapter, I will tell you all ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is cracking that goes to war, and another when sharpening, as with the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if at cracking with injury, and cracking throughout a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its tool and its own proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes into his mind; and he knows that bone breakage is perceived by when the limb is twisted, opens well outward, and gets squeezed under the hand; and when there is no twist or touchiness, and the patient doesn't feel much pain, if there's no breakage; but it can still have twists, cracks, or small breakages.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the following remedies, and then gradually tighten it now in a subtle manner.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that when the breaking occurred in action, and the two parts were separated, you must now place them equally, just like you would with incisions or wounds; and if the incisions are healing smoothly, then let no day pass until those incisions have healed; only then can you adjust them slightly and wisely. And know that their restoration is easier than those that had pieces; then restrain it, as described below this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is divided into two parts, whether they are hands or feet, or close to your hand as smaller limbs, or at two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the injured parts of the limb have healed, you reposition them through all means in their places with the movements you can, and remember that through your actions do not cause injury or pain to the patient; and adjust both ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it is done beautifully, and do not strain too much, not pressing as those do when they extract pus and muscle tension in the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in place, properly restrain the patient so they do not move them, neither while awake nor asleep, nor when turning or in any other manner; and ensure that the limb is secure enough to feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when he feels no pain, it is not quite in the right position. It should be placed in such a way that there is no pain felt and ensure it is put correctly so that there is no twist upon its restoration; and the quality of the broken member must agree with what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied in smallness and size, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And for small limbs, like arms and legs, and those similar: it should be wrapped in soft and fine linen; for larger ones, like breasts and thighs: they should be wrapped with a broad and firm band because the wide bands encompass the entire large limb and compress it evenly from all sides so there is no twist; then bind it with light ligatures, three or four according to the limb, and press your hand slightly along the entire band, then go above the fracture and compress less, allowing the fracture to move away a little; and soften the band gradually until you have reached a large part of the healthy part, then take another band and bind around the broken part. Then return to the area below the fracture and compress moderately, neither too hard nor too softly as we have explained above; then place linen or cloth bands between the ligature bands until they are all even, then secure everything with a belt on top, and then put your well-made pins in place if there is pus or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or pus, apply something soothing for pus extraction and which reduces the swelling, leaving it thus for a few days; then begin to extract your stars, being half the width of a slender reed cut evenly, or from the staff used to make lances, or from palm fronds, and do this according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the stars which one puts on for breaking are somewhat larger and wider than others; they should also be as long as needed according to the size of the limb, whether small or large. Then pull them on the stars just like you did in the first instance during the breakage, then tie a complementary thread above it, similarly to how you tied in the first instance around the breakage area; make them tighter now and less so later. And it must be that the threads are medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be made of soft linen because if the thread is thick, as they do when making their thread for sewing with linen cords, and this is a great mistake, since the tie cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it does not fit that there is less than two dimes' width between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are burned by the marks of the pins after the constriction in their health, then put patches of linen or shredded wool on them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is burned and the joints are broken, I will tell you the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to restrain all broken limbs for the entire first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to apply these plasters immediately after three or seven days or longer depending on the severity of any subsequent abscesses occurring; and here is the way the ancient plastering methods were used to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that stays at the mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg and create a mixture not too thin nor too thick. Apply this concoction carefully, it is the common method for restoring fractures in various positions, even for women and young children, as neither the process is overly harsh nor excessively cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for applying plaster to restore fractures and dislocations: take 30 raisins, dainy apples, rue, and asafetida, along with gum Arabic and mastic, each in an amount of .x.3; myrrh and aloes in amounts of .v.3; vinegar at seven parts out of eight. Make a powder from these ingredients and mix them with plenty of egg. If the consistency of the mixture is warm, use this plaster. It has a good composition, quickly restores broken bones, and is worth more than many remedies for men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering suitable for torsion: take mugwort and valerian root, in quantity of ten parts; myrrh and aloes, in quantity of nine parts; stonework (possibly meant to be acaica or some local herb), six parts; boric acid from Armenia, ten parts. Crush them well together, mix with water or plenty of egg whites, and apply it as required.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for dressing wounds and fractures, and alleviating the pain that arises, and they cut bone and cause abrasion: take new wool, and moisten it in a mixture of oil and heated fat, and place it on the wound area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Dressing wounds doesn't heal them completely, but it's better for soothing abscesses and properly handling bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for plastering which restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial dogwood leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for dressing, in the restoration of bone breakage and to soothe the process of pus drainage.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vismarrow, chamomile, violet flowers, ground almonds, from each take one part; and grind them, mix with wine, if your limbs are heated, mix with wet coriander water, or water alone, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method for more forceful plastering than the first one, when hard pus comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and lin seed, balauste, melilot, and sansuce, and violet and chamomile flowers from all these take one part; grind and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ippocrates instructs that for restoring strength to a broken limb, one should apply a balm made of wax and oil, and nothing else more. He states it should be neither too soft nor too hard but in between the two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests applying something to the broken limb for restoration, things that are dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mussels and omelets' feathers or bird feathers, and basil, and lime of equal size, grind them, make a paste from it, and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor move its bone in place; if you do not loosen it with your hands And when pain comes to the limb, or itchiness, without rest or swelling, if this happens, quickly, and loosen it, and replace the plaster now; then use a light cloth and wet sponge, dip them into water, and raise the limb until the itch stops, and soothe any pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then place on dried wool, moistened with water or rose oil, and secure it with a bandage, until you are sure of the pus coming out hot; and subdue the inflammation in the limb, and rid of the pain, then resume gentle reattachment, and a little plaster, but do not apply pressure as before; and with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus is yellow and red, pain, swelling are present, indicating an abscess throughout, then you need plaster and binding, start again as you did the first time equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there is nothing of what we have said affecting the member, or if it cannot be dislocated until after three or four or five or seven days; and each time leave it for twenty days according to this custom, as long as the injury heals, and brings the adaptation of flesh up; then increase the restraint more than before, and let its meat grow back, just as I said previously; and if you see that the skin dries too much, know that nothing can come out; start with hot water each time you dislocate it, and do this every third day, cleanse a bit of the wound; through this means then remove the injury from the member, speed up whatever local surgeons are doing, that revert the member in wrong position: this is bad practice, and such are ugly operations; I see nothing else than to let it heal straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	regarding various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes. Their causes are distinct; for there are fractures produced by the impact of a sword, and breaks in the neck completely crush the bone up to the symphysis that separates one bone from another, like when a boar tusk or spear hits it. This is why this method of fracture is called "haunching".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword penetrates through the bone from above without piercing it, and this is called a "complete" fracture; and the injuries caused by these two kinds of fractures are either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack, or break in the bone, or under a stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture up to the membrane that is under the bone or above it, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that heals within the bone as thin as hair, and has a small crack, this type of fracture is called "hairline". And if the wound is made by striking with stone or falling, or from some other object, and it causes part of the bone to enter the body cavity, like when candle makers work on candles; if one were to drop stones into the containers.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This often happens in those who have wet bones beneath, such as the skull of children; it occurs through all these methods of fracture where small fragments are released like maggots; and I will speak more about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all methods of breaks through the removal above them, and the investigation on stakes, and by the putrid flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed inside it, revealing the dark break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a break, beware of adverse effects from the malady, and if you observe no harmful incident such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, pallor, fever, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents, and you hope for salvation, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when snow first comes to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fifteenth day since you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day so that the pus under the bone may be rotten, and bring about the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if bone breaking reaches until the membrane covering the brain, then it is necessary that you cut through the broken part like this: and take hold of the bone's fracture edge, and uncover onto the bone in every way you can, and on the shape of the wound as much as you can, and if bleeding begins to reveal the bone, or pus appears, use what is needed there, and fill up the space with wet cloth in rose oil; then let the wound rest until the pus has subsided and bleeding has ceased; only then begin through the bone to remove, which is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut at a narrow angle forward, and this is its shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have many different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of hard iron; and in operation lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, it is necessary that you pierce inside, in such a way that you perform cuts with needles, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the thickness of the flesh, and there should be a margin above the point about 1 inch, ensuring the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each goes to its place under the thickness of the bone, having needles for all parts; and this is the form of the three ways of using needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce through the bone is that you place one needle on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know the bone is pierced. Then replace the needle a little later elsewhere, and do so throughout, then scrape out the space of the bone between the roots of teeth as precisely as possible, and do this more finely than you can, gently, as we have said, as long as you are able to remove the bone with your hands or any instruments you have like forceps, pliers; and make sure not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is necessary that you remove any remaining preparation from the bone to all other instruments similar to a file. But it must be more robust and finer than the other file; and if there remains nothing of small bones or no scales, then gently scrape with one of these tools; afterwards treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is as Galien said, which is safer; and it involves applying a strong lard, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you should uncover part of the bone, at or near where the break is made and moves, so when you have uncovered that part, place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision tool, as it's shown here.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, and make the incision go across in two parts so it faces the bone; then start cutting with a small mallet above, making sure you lightly touch the entire bone, being careful of the tissue surrounding it; if it sticks to the bone, gently remove it, because you will remove the bone without causing harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not puncture until it touches the tissue and only the bone is cut from above, and there are small pieces left, then after that roughness, you should scrape off the scales with a fine shaver you must have various sizes, in order to apply the most suitable for each part according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before great razors, and afterwards of finer tools, and do not stop doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other haircutting and subtle breaking tasks, you should adjust the work according to its position; this is something that cannot be answered by someone who has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, it should be that you use a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, soak in oil and apply it onto the wound. Then take another doubled cloth with two or three layers, soak it in wine and oil, and place it over the first layer; do this more gently than possible without causing discomfort to the wound. Afterward, administer another bandage from above, not using too much force that it only touches the wound. Leave like this for one or two days until the abscesses are less inflamed, then remove the bandages and apply medications such as thyme roots, wheat flour, incense powder, and wormwood, among other things; make a powder from these and put it on the wound, and administer regular medicines without causing irritation. Take care to keep the wound clean, do not leave any ointment or allow it to coagulate; because when blood clots form on the brain tissue, they will spread and harm the patient; as soon as you apply something corrosive to the wound, it spreads from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, should any unfortunate events befall the patient as we have described, it is with doubt and without fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if illness does not come out only through the medicine we've placed there, should it have that effect, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of roset oil and a drapel of glue, then put this on his face; then you will treat him in ways suitable for treatment until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts above the nose are never broken, or only one is broken if you do so, because they consist of two bones; and this lower part is cartilaginous, it doesn't break, nor does it weaken from twisting or bending, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must pinch your little finger or beneath your nose, and place that break evenly inside your index finger, and outwards at the nostril hole, until the nose revives according to its natural form; and do this gently, and be careful not for the patient to feel pain through your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose part and cannot reach to the place on the head, then it is necessary that you put it at an equal distance from the tip of a somewhat thick reed.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, redo this procedure, and try to restore on the first day if possible; if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has been relieved, then pinch at the nose tip with linen cloth pieces, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you pull two from another side, if breaking occurs; and let the threads be so thick that they fill the little hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no one should moisten their wicks with butter, and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I believe it might not be correct, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a mixture from an egg yolk and powder of mill; then leave the wick until the bone is hard and the cartilage toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes use goose feathers instead of threads, and if with one egg you cover the inside, and keep it warm, and blow into the wound, do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscesses come to the nose in the same way as you handle them, put a wad of moistened wax or cotton in olive oil, or in a pot of snail juice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus comes out, apply a poultice on the outside, made from ashes' powder and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place it on light sticks and don't bind them tightly; and if the stick breaks into small pieces, and they break into small pieces, you should use tools suitable for this purpose, then cut along the wound, and cure it with various remedies, joining them together, using bandages and ointments suitable for this; and if there's no wound under the sticks, cure the wick, and leave the treatment of wicks until they're healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured internally and there's no wound visible from the outside, and only the breakage is external, not shattered within. It doesn't crack into two halves but breaks internally, so it's easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the fracture occurs in the right part, you should press your index finger into the mouth near the jawbone. And if the fracture is in the left mandible, then use your right hand's index finger and press it gently into the inside of the injury, and do this with the other hand from the outside, making sure to do so evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is complete and affects both sides (.i.e., left and right), it is necessary that you administer an equal extension on both parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And when the movements of the teeth occur, or a rupture, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk. Then place on the broken jaw pieces of beeswax, and put under one doubled piece of cloth; then on the cloth put a large candle properly made, or a piece of leather equal in size to the length and width of the jaw. Secure it in such manner that you can, command the patient to rest, and eat small pieces of light meat.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie on the third day, and then adjust what has become undone; apply plaster, made with powder from a mill mixed generously with eggs or flour of almond meal, after removing the beeswax; then place under the plaster light wool, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's position does not change, let it be for as long as they are healing. Many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if you encounter pus-filled sores, then follow what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, reward nothing of the bone that has been removed; such delicacy requires tools suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains nothing, if the wound is wide, place one dressing suitable for it over it, to promote healing, until it has healed.
de la forcele	by the power
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie. de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the fracture of the hand bone
