And if abscesses do form, let the treatment continue for another day, until the abscess is relieved, and don't disturb it on the third or fourth day either, as you would be causing harm with that.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you see the bone has broken out from under its skin, it is necessary that you place it gently in your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the limbs don't allow you to place them evenly in your hands, then use this iron tool with it, which is made of iron and has a length of seven or six inches, and its width should match the size of the wound; for each fracture treatment, the surgeon must have three or four of these tools according to his need; they should be round and slightly thick, so that they don't bend under compression on your limb when you work, and they should be sharp in front, and rounded in the middle towards the front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called 'palanché', because it is necessary that the bent shoulders be placed on the tip of the visible bone; and hold it in place once, until it heals, and be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the tools cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you hold the tip of the bone, as long as the tools have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you can't return the bone back, as we have said, if you have an instrument suitable for this purpose, or a scalpel or surgeon's knife, in your power; then cut into the bone that is stuck within it with roughness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and after the patient feels intense pain, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you aim to place it back in its natural position, then smear the wound with a black and thick wine. If done properly when it's in such state; and do not apply any ointment or other thing that might cause oiliness, which could lead to infection and corruption on the wound; instead, ensure no such thing results from this action. After setting the bone back into place, administer herbs as you see fit after restoring the bone, keep the wound open, cover it completely according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not tightened up by the pressure from the covering; many have done this mistake in the past and led to death or corrosion on the patient's body. Ensure that the tightness of the bandage is softer than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that harmful accidents might have taken place, as we said earlier, and should find pain in your arm, then it would not be suitable to apply ointments; but cover internally, instead of applying ointments, wrap with hard cloths, and fasten them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is healing, remove what you have applied with all the wine, and then put on a healing ointment for wounds, such as the fourfold medicine and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary for the limb to be bandaged in such a way that the joint slides easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal anymore right away, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so it is necessary for you to treat the wound with a tent, and remove all these pieces causing discomfort, which bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the arm or any other way of decay, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he said in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed in the limb, like the bone of the elbow or shoulder, or others similar to large bones, you should not treat it immediately because many die from it, but let it heal by itself until it becomes putrid. By chance, it might drain on its own after about 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if possible; and if you cannot, leave it as it is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The blows come many times after the healing of the wound, especially when it's near the joint. And there is much to see in the shape of the limb; and by chance cannot perform its natural actions on the limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when it comes to such things: if you give him/her stiffening medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarsaparilla, senna, and similar others, do so according to which of these you choose or all together, mixing them with stinking wine or enough eggs or milk; then apply them on the knot in poultices, press well and don't remove it with your hands day by day; then reset it, and start again another one until the knots are removed. Or apply pressure onto a piece of wood well made; because the properties of wood is such that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the knot has hardened into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, cover it with a bandage, showing the excessness clearly visible; or take it off to any barber until it's removed, then continue the treatment until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb that is weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: because one was tied too tightly and wasn't tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and they couldn't breathe properly on the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or due to too large movements not in their time; or because he lacks blood in his body, being weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat the herbs, and make their body soft until the swelling multiplies within them; then give them baths, and bring them joy and rest. Afterward, apply grease to the limb so that the grease attracts to the major swelling, and wash it often with lukewarm water until the swelling aligns with the limb; and restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If a limb is bent after an injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after being put back in place, and if the bones have been broken apart, and though the shape of the limb is distorted, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who say that one must break the entire limb anew; many such actions are done in our land. These practices are criticized and result in severe harms and even death; however, when the swelling and pain are still fresh, they should be treated with hot water or with herbs that soften tissue, like mint leaves, roots, and thyme, etc.; and one should apply a moistening plaster, such as well-made duck fat, and take the essence of mint and mix it with lard or oil from sesame, then make a plaster. Alternatively, take greased figs and grind them with cornmeal and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the node removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Let there be gentle movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and durable, like bone, and requires being treated with metal, so that it reaches up to the bone, one should do this gently at the precise point of incision. And include consideration and study in the treatment process.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, because it cannot move there anymore, and the limb is incorrectly positioned, causing great pain and injury to the body.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens without any reason, if it fits now to bring back without disturbing anything.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if you delay, it will swell the limbs, and by chance put pressure on the joints; in this way there should not move the limb when it is swollen: many times bring pus and other pains. Nevertheless, whenever this happens, have a surgeon treat the patient, then leave him alone until all the abscesses subside; then immerse the member in hot water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and cure each member as they come into their own place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat connected to their places and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and causing saliva from the mouth not to be contained, nor able to close his mouth, and wrapping his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is complete and accomplished, it should be treated promptly without hesitation; and in such a way that the servants cut the head of the patient near the disease site, and hold the pins in his pocket in the root of the dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be outside the hands for adjustment; command the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers are kept equally placed until it regains its position in place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it causes pain, similarly when these two jaws are together, using hot water and oil, as long as gently resetting them; do not overly force the reset, just as we said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back equally, and the mouth of the sick man is well closed after being mollified, you should put on wet cloths as poultices made from rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with moist threads; and make the sick person lie down facing their back, and have their limbs situated between two cushions so they don't move neither to the right nor to the left, nor even attempt to chew, but should only consume light food until the pains are relieved and the jaws are stitched; and then feed them what they desire lightly, without trying to open their mouth during eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and restored.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly set in one hour and are not returned to their original position, they lead to fevers and chronic discomfort, and by chance stomach release, and by chance vomiting of pure contents.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times death befalls the one to whom it happens, within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the lever principle
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve from within the continuation of it and from its back, and is dislocated only once outside, and one feels this well indeed.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the healing process is as follows: The sick person lies on their back and extends their arms. Then they are positioned in a shape resembling your hand, which will eventually return to its place. After this, place them on plaster and bind them up, then firmly press them together; and if they dislocate again from their front side, you must reset them into their original position as we've explained previously. After that, place them back onto the plaster and wrap them up, pressing tightly, while instructing the patient to rest until they are completely healed; by this method the shoulder joints of the back are also brought back when they have been reset from their location.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways: one way is when it dislocates towards the back of the socket; and the second is at the bottom part of the joint; and occasionally dislocating above the socket, this happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inward for the nerves; and several times dislocates downwards towards the socket, even in those with little flesh, because they jump quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it jumps on points, and returns into the points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men due to percussion or cracking, and the shoulder swells with an inflamed abscess, and they think that it is dislocated from this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Thus, you must verify it as long as you are certain about it; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that when the shoulder is dislocated downwards towards the socket, there's an obvious difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one; you'll find various distinctions in them. You will see a depression at the top of the shoulder and from the socket to the neck of the shoulder as if it were another one; also, the patient cannot bring their hand back to their nose nor move by any means; similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it isn't concealed either since you find it clearly at the neck; this way of dislocation can only be cured when it's new, or when there was a lack of care for the patient.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is: the surgeon raises his hand above the illness, then places his fingers on the elbow and lifts the joint to full height at the top of the body; and the surgeon raises his hand and extends it upwards, then puts it under; if it comes too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come about as we said earlier within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and have them stretch out, soothing and relieving any pain, such as decoction from garlic and fenugreek and marjoram in hot water, and they should take this treatment. Then place bandages on their back, and underneath one's buttocks put a cushion of even size, neither too soft nor too hard; then place the heel of one's hand under the cushion, and lift the head from the shoulder gently, and pull the hand away from the patient; and other assistants should sharpen the tip of the hand of the patient so it doesn't move backwards; this shoulder has now returned to its normal position, and if you see that you are pulling it back in this manner: then let there be someone who is larger than the patient present at home; stand straight towards their side, and place your shoulder underneath the cushion of the patient, lift the cushion upwards so the patient hangs in an 'A'; and other assistants should pull the hand away from the patient's back towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so it can carry no weight, then the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the method of resetting is also done in other ways: one sticks the long stick into the ground so that the shoulder sits like a nail, and it should neither be too big nor too slippery; then place this under the patient but with leaves above, and make sure the leaves cover fully along the length of the stick; and have the part of the stick with the handle on top. Then extend your hand from below on the other side in this formation, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it doesn't return due to all these things as we've said, perform this treatment: take a piece of wood that is two arms long by three inches wide, which has the handle large enough for it to fit into the socket fully from above according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie it on the top of the stick with a sheet underneath, so that the stick does not irritate the wound; then place it onto the socket towards the wound; and extend your arm up to the stick from its tip, and fix the shoulder support onto the stick, and the arm at the base of the hand, then put the arm down on one pole as long as half a span wide, and let the other hand hang down now; the joint will return in this position.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, no matter how, should you need to place upon the joint a thread that's even, then apply plastered with powdered mill grain, along with incense and yolk of egg, across all the shoulder and around it, then remove from the joint addition, and tie back on the plaster, and wrap the hand in its neck. And let your hands stay like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it should be that he eats a little, until the limbs are strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved due to moisture or some other reason that caused it to move, then you should apply three cauterizations to it, as was explained in our previous chapter about cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't stay in place, and can't lift your arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is damaged or extended or weakened; and know that the joint would never be properly fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are near the buttocks and breasts, or behind, if caused by pushing and stretching of hands, are administered in other places; treatment should be applied as long as it remains clean.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes stiffness in the limb, and late movements, then apply hot baths many times, until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the shoulder joint's dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points and returns to these points; and if it has been dislocated from all directions, equally in front and behind, then dislocation cannot be fully restored, for you can see this clearly and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the metal of the cut with the healthy part, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and you cannot bend or touch the arm to either side.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it in this way that the abscesses are close to heal, because if they were healed too quickly, it would be a problem to bring them back; and sometimes cannot be brought back completely, even when it's behind; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and in consequence death may come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is like this when one can return it to its normal state: you extend your patient's hand with both of yours; and his arms are spread outwards and downwards, and his hands are placed in front according to the length of the forearm, forwards, backwards, and sideways, then you push the joint towards his wrist area or at the base of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he holds both his hands together, and pushes with the base of his palm against the knife that is stuck out.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it doesn't return to its original position, apply strong extension; and when you do this, extend the arm with both hands, and keep the other hand on it, so that it does not move during extension. Then, bend the arm in all directions, once you've wrapped a doubled piece of long and wide cloth around it; and when you attempt to join the joint back together using your hand, apply oil for softening purposes before this is done. After properly joining them, make sure they remain joined until they reattach naturally; once they are in place, cover with dry plaster mixed with egg whites, shape it appropriately, and allow the arm to hang by its side near the wound. Leave it like this for a few days before removing the bandage.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, remove the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint isn't set well, redo the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like that for some days, until it's firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels chilled after the repositioning of the joint, and it moves again, bathe and scrub it well, press until it is relieved. Or you place a layer of fatty sheep's wool on the joint for one day and a night, then remove the flesh, and let them take a bath; when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put back the wool, and then enter the bath; and so do this two or three times until it feels well; and if you see fit, place a damp cow's skin heated with butter on it, then apply pressure; if it returns to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose. Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi. Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you can't move it well, and there's no fracture, then apply warm water, and rub it until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	From the dislocation of the fingers of the hand

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	With ankle dislocation or back.

I say that in the case of a belly wound coming forward towards the groin, nothing heals; and similarly when it comes directly to either side, one cannot cure anything but what is precisely where it goes behind, as I say; and let the patient's wounds be stretched out over his/her body equally on the backside, making sure they do not bruise. des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, somewhat dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the understanding of his dislocation internally is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the diseased knee than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot double their knee joint in the fire; and those limbs are swollen due to abscess beneath them because the thigh bone comes to them.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who approaches death, if it is that this event is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who approaches before [death], if it is that his leg is well according to completion; nevertheless, he does not even double the knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and he retains his urine, and swells up the ankle, and when he walks, he goes on tiptoe.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who approaches behind [death], if it is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more bent than the other, and the ankle becomes soft, and the shoulder of the hip moves under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedy for this appearance of dislocation is that you should confirm whether the dislocation is old and stays in its position, if there is no treatment; and it does not benefit to assume anything.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those in which the dislocation is recent, there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to correct it and stretch inside and outside, and move to the right and left; should it return successfully, requiring no other treatment afterwards.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans. Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of stretching is common for four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres. And if you cannot secure it in this way as we have said, then bind the two feet of the affected person together with a strong bandage around both heels and both knees; make sure that the affected leg is stretched out more than the other by about two arms' length. Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it does not work to extend the diseased leg backwards or lift it off the ground. Instead, the patient should lie in such a way that they are like when their hip was dislocated at the back as we have described about lying on both hips; and he lies on his chest, and the line is extended as we previously mentioned, and one must press to the joint on the table; it's done right when the leg extends and they are equal; then adjust the buttocks, place the plaster, and apply pressure with a bandage, so that the hip does not move. And he should rest for three or four days, then release him, and put plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, reapply the pressure as before, and let him rest for three more days; then release him, and make him walk properly until his limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways: this means, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the symptoms are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if they cannot reach their knee, know that it is dislocated; and all treatments consist of having the patient sit upright, extend their leg if possible, place your back against their buttocks, and place their foot on yours; then hold their knee between your palms, pull it between your fingers, then bend both sides from the knee tightly; and another assistant should spread their foot out until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that they gently reach well into their knee; and apply the plaster, make the leg rest against the knee, keep everything tight for three or four days, then release; and do not disturb the patient's activities while their limbs are still weak.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, apply strong extension, as we said in the treatment of the hip, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never completely reset and still remain in or out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it attempts to move before reaching the point where it has dislocated: the realignment should be gentle, and one must gently extend it with their hands as soon as it's slightly in place.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is slightly dislocated, you should make the patient lie straight and hold their leg straight out by their side with your hands above the ankle. Then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then with your left two times, followed by extending it upwards, and firmly push the foot upwards; do this two times while pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start working on it again because it will return; and if it can't return like this, you should displace the patient so they are lying on their back on the ground, firmly place one peg in the earth between their buttocks, and tie cloths around them to prevent chafing; then cut the clothes near the ankle of both legs, and another person holds the foot with their hands or at a rope tied to the neck below the foot; then extend each person's hands equally, and put the peg firmly between the patient's buttocks so that it retains the leg when stretched; finally place the dislocated parts in line with your hands, and another person cuts the healthy leg just above the ankle, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it's at the right point, place the plaster and apply the bandage on top, hold it tightly in position, and fasten the boot to the leg. Make sure not to tie the ligaments behind the ankle too tight; then leave it for two or three days. If the ligament gets loose, untie it. Then remove the bandage after three days or a week, and gently guide the patient for another four days; if they proceed beyond this period, there is no certainty that further dislocation will not occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you find pus coming out, then it is necessary to soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it heals.

Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is at no point on the back or bottom of the foot, it's necessary that you make the patient sit straight with their full leg or on a table completely upright, and place your foot on what opens from these joints. Then press against your foot firmly until they feel it. And when it feels equal, and there is nothing opening up, then put under the sole of the foot a bench for shoulders, then apply firm pressure, and let it rest for three days, then release; and make them rest until they are well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound occurs along with dislocation and the intention is to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in your treatment if you are inexperienced in this art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and slow, do not be hasty; at the beginning use soothing things that remove abscesses, and leave the patient to God's mercy if you see no hope of recovery; and when you see there is hope, immediately reset the limb back in its place, as if the abscesses would disappear; and once the limb is back in place, administer soothing things that remove abscesses, treat the wound appropriately with desiccated remedies; and if due to dislocation it involves fracture and small bones are exposed, set them and do as we have advised in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I've said, because this is judged according to your Creator, and for the wisdom you arm yourself with and protect your body.
